Compound and Simple Ignorance in Ibn Taymiyya
Ibn Taymiyya defines two types of ignorance using Quranic parables.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish compound ignorance from simple ignorance, and explain why compound ignorance necessarily entails simple ignorance using the Quranic parables.

Core Idea
Compound ignorance: a mirage of knowledge; simple ignorance: darkness without claim.

Ibn Taymiyya uses two Quranic parables to explain the nature of disbelief (kufr) and ignorance (jahl). Recognizing the difference between compound ignorance (believing falsehood to be truth) and simple ignorance (no knowledge at all) is crucial for evaluating theological claims and understanding deviant beliefs. This lesson dissects these concepts as presented in the passage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of ignorance
From the passage, extract the two types: compound ignorance (al-jahl al-murakkab) and simple ignorance (al-jahl al-basit). Note their descriptions: compound is like a mirage, simple is darkness.
Compound ignorance involves a false claim to knowledge; simple ignorance is absence.
2
Extract the defining features of compound ignorance
Compound ignorance is when a person thinks they know something, but what they think they know is false and non-existent. The heart is thirsty for truth but finds only illusion.
This resembles the mirage (sarāb) parable from Quran.
3
Extract the defining features of simple ignorance
Simple ignorance is the absence of knowledge and guidance—no truth is evident, no guidance is seen. It is like being in darkness.
No false belief accompanies simple ignorance; it is pure lack.
4
Understand the relationship between the two
Ibn Taymiyya states: 'Compound disbelief entails simple disbelief, and every disbelief necessarily contains compound ignorance.' This means compound ignorance includes simple ignorance as a component—if you have a false belief, you are also ignorant of the truth.
One cannot have compound ignorance without also lacking true knowledge (simple ignorance).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحدهما : مَثَل الكفر والجهل المركَّب الذي يحسَبه صاحبه موجودا، ويكون خيالا معدوما كالسراب، والقلب عطشان إلى الحقِّ كَعَطَشِ الجسد إلى الماء، فإذا طلب ما ظنّه ماءً وجدَه سرابا، ووجد الله عنده فوفاه حسابه، والله سريع الحساب. وهكذا تجد عامة هؤلاء الخارجين عن السنة والجماعة. والمَثَل الثاني: مَثَل الكفر والجهل البسيط الذي لا يتبيَّن فيه حق ولا يُرى فيه هدى. والكفرُ المركَّبُ مستلزم للبسيط، وكلُّ كفر فلا بد فيه من جهل مركّب. فضرب سبحانه المَثَلين بذلك ليبيّن حال الاعتقاد الفاسد، ويبين حال عدم معرفة الحق، وهو يُشْبِهُ حال المغضوب عليهم والضالين، حال المصمِّم على الباطل حتى يحلَّ به العذاب وحال الضال الذي لا يرى طريق الهدى. فنسأل الله العظيم أن يثبتنا بالقول الثابت في الحياة الدنيا والآخرة، وأن يرزقنا الاعتصام بالكتاب والسنة.
One is the example of compound disbelief and ignorance (jahl murakkab) that its possessor thinks exists, but it is a non-existent illusion like a mirage; the heart is thirsty for truth as the body is thirsty for water. So when he seeks what he thinks is water, he finds a mirage, and finds Allah with him who gives him his account in full, and Allah is swift in account. Thus you find the generality of those who deviate from the Sunnah and the community. The second example: the example of simple disbelief and ignorance in which no truth is evident and no guidance is seen. Compound disbelief entails simple disbelief, and every disbelief necessarily contains compound ignorance. So He, glorified, struck the two examples to clarify the state of corrupt belief, and to clarify the state of ignorance of truth, and it resembles the state of those who have incurred [Allah's] wrath and those who are astray: the state of the one who insists on falsehood until punishment befalls him, and the state of the one who is astray and sees no path of guidance. So we ask Allah the Almighty to keep us firm with the firm word in this life and the Hereafter, and to grant us adherence to the Book and the Sunnah.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage defines two types of ignorance (jahl) and disbelief (kufr): compound and simple. Ibn Taymiyya uses two parables from the Quran: the mirage (sarāb) for compound ignorance, and darkness for simple ignorance. Compound ignorance is when a person thinks he knows something but it is false — like a mirage. His heart is thirsty for truth but he finds nothing. Simple ignorance is complete lack of knowledge, like being in darkness without any light. The author then states that compound disbelief necessarily entails simple disbelief, meaning that every compound ignorance includes simple ignorance. He concludes with a supplication for steadfastness.

Key Terms
الجهل المركب
الجهل البسيط
السراب
الكفر المركب
الكفر البسيط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what does compound ignorance (al-jahl al-murakkab) resemble?
A) A mirage that appears as water but is nothing
B) Complete darkness
C) A thirsty person finding water
D) The state of the people of the Book

Key Takeaway
Compound ignorance is a false claim to knowledge that necessarily involves simple ignorance of the truth, as illustrated by the Quranic parable of the mirage.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify whether each scenario describes compound or simple ignorance: (a) A person who rejects the prophethood of Muhammad after hearing clear proofs and argues against them. (b) A person living in a remote area who has never heard of Islam. Explain your reasoning using the definitions from this passage.
?
Using the mirage analogy, explain how compound ignorance includes simple ignorance. Then give an example from Islamic history of a group that exhibited compound ignorance.

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Fabricated Hadiths and False Claims to Secret Knowledge
Ibn Taymiyya critiques false attributions to righteous shaykhs and fabricated hadiths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of false attribution Ibn Taymiyya lists and critically assess the use of fabricated hadiths to support claims of 'direct inspiration'.

Core Idea
Fabricated hadiths and distorted words of shaykhs are used to claim knowledge beyond the prophets.

This passage from Ibn Taymiyya’s Naqd al-Mantiq continues his critique of deviant epistemologies. He moves from logical errors to real-world examples: how some Sufis and followers of shaykhs fabricate or distort statements to claim a privileged access to truth, even above the prophets. By dissecting these false attributions, Ibn Taymiyya teaches us how to spot illegitimate evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of false attribution
Ibn Taymiyya lists several origins: lies, misinterpreted ambiguous speech, slips, sins. Note each category and how they relate to the shaykhs' actual statements.
2
Recognize the claim of special knowledge
Look at how groups claim exclusive 'secrets and realities' (asrar wa haqa'iq) that even messengers did not claim. They demand submission without questioning.
3
Spot the fabricated hadith
The example about Umar and the Zanjī. How does this hadith function as evidence for their claim? Ibn Taymiyya labels it as fabricated (mawdu'a).
4
Analyze the implied epistemology
They claim knowledge by 'what is cast into the heart' (ilqa' fi al-qalb). Why does Ibn Taymiyya reject this? Because it bypasses prophetic transmission.
5
Connect to the broader critique
How does this fit into Ibn Taymiyya's overall project of defending prophetic knowledge as the standard? The critique is part of his attack on false sources of knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أمثلة ذلك ما ينسبه كثيرٌ من أتباع المشايخ والصوفية إلى المشايخ الصَّادقين من الكذب والمحال، أو يكون من كلامهم المتشابه الذي تأولوه على غير تأويله، أو يكون من غلطات بعض الشيوخ وزلاتهم، أو من ذنوب بعضهم وخطئهم، مثل كثير من البدع والفجور الذي يفعله بعضهم بتأويل سائغ أو بوجه غير سائغ، فيعفى عنه، أو يتوب، أو يكون منه ومن غيره حسنات يُغفر له بها ، أو مصائب يكفّر عنه بها، أو يكون من كلام المتشبهين بأولياء الله من ذوي الزهادات والعبادات والمقالات، وليس هو من أولياء الله المتقين بل من الجاهلين الظالمين المعتدين أو المنافقين أو الكافرين. وهذا كثيرٌ مِلْءُ العالم، تجـد كـل قـوم يـدعـون مــن الاختصاص بالأسرار والحقائق ما لا يدَّعي المرسلون، وأن ذلك عند خواصهم، وأن ذلك لا يقابل إلا بالتسليم، ويحتجون لذلك بأحاديث موضوعة وتفسيرات باطلة، مثل قولهم عن عمر : ( إن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يتحدث هو وأبو بكر بحديث وكنتُ كالزنجي بينهما )، فيجعلون عمر مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وصديقه كالزنجي ، وهو حاضر يسمعُ الكلام، ثم يدَّعي أحدهم أنه عَلِمَ ذلك بما قُذِفَ في قلبه! ويدعي كل منهم أن ذلك هو ما يقوله من الزور والباطل.
Examples of that include what many followers of shaykhs and Sufis attribute to truthful shaykhs of lies and absurdities, or from their ambiguous speech which they interpreted in other than its true interpretation, or from slips and mistakes of some shaykhs, or from their sins and errors, like many innovations and immoralities that some commit with a permissible interpretation or an impermissible way, so they are forgiven, or they repent, or they have good deeds that cause forgiveness, or afflictions that expiate. Or it may be from the speech of those who pretend to be awliya of Allah among those with asceticism, worship, and sayings, while they are not from the pious awliya of Allah but rather from the ignorant oppressors or hypocrites or disbelievers. This is abundant, filling the world. You find every group claiming special access to secrets and realities that not even the messengers claimed, and that this is for their elite, and that it must be accepted with submission, and they argue with fabricated hadiths and false interpretations, like their statement about Umar: 'The Prophet (PBUH) was conversing with Abu Bakr and I was like a Zanjī between them.' So they make Umar with the Prophet and his friend like a Zanjī, while he was present hearing the speech. Then one of them claims he knows that by what was cast into his heart! And each of them claims that his falsehood and lies are the truth.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage critiques the practice of some Sufis and followers of shaykhs who attribute false statements to righteous shaykhs, misinterpret their words, or exaggerate their slips. Ibn Taymiyya categorizes these attributions: lies, misinterpreted ambiguous speech, mistakes, sins, etc. He then addresses a more severe phenomenon: groups who claim exclusive knowledge of secrets and realities, even greater than what the prophets claimed, and they demand unquestioning acceptance. They support their claims with fabricated hadiths, such as the false story about Umar being like a Zanjī (a black person) while the Prophet and Abu Bakr conversed. This story is used to justify that knowledge is acquired by 'what is cast into the heart' (ilqā' fī al-qalb). Ibn Taymiyya exposes this as falsehood.

Key Terms
أحاديث موضوعة
المتشابه
إلقاء في القلب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do groups who claim special knowledge demand from others?
A) Rational proof
B) Submission without questioning
C) Debate
D) Financial support

Key Takeaway
False attributions and fabricated hadiths are used to elevate human claims above prophetic knowledge; critiquing them is essential for sound epistemology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find a contemporary claim of 'direct inspiration' (ilqa') used to justify a religious practice. Examine whether it relies on fabricated or weak hadiths.
?
In a group discussion, take the role of Ibn Taymiyya and refute the claim that Umar was like a Zanjī, using the criteria of hadith criticism.

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of False Spiritual Authority
Ibn Taymiyya categorizes and refutes various false claims of spiritual secrets and authority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three categories of false spiritual claimants critiqued by Ibn Taymiyya (elevating poetry over the Quran, claiming union with the divine, and anthropomorphism) and evaluate his method of refutation using fabricated hadith and revealed doctrine.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya exposes false spiritual authority by showing its reliance on fabricated texts and heretical doctrines.

Ibn Taymiyya's critique here is not a blanket rejection of spiritual experience but a precise identification of those who exceed the bounds of Islam. He distinguishes the truthful shaykhs from false claimants who misinterpret ambiguous speech, commit sins, or imitate the awliya while being ignorant or disbelievers. He then gives three concrete categories of heretical practices: elevating poetry above the Quran, claiming union (ittihad) with the divine, and anthropomorphizing God. This lesson will help you recognize these patterns and understand his method of exposing falsehood.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and target
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice that Ibn Taymiyya begins by distinguishing truthful shaykhs from false claimants. Who is he critiquing? List the categories of false claimants mentioned in the first paragraph.
2
List the sources of false claims
Ibn Taymiyya enumerates several origins of false claims: ambiguous speech misinterpreted, mistakes, sins, and imitation by the ignorant, unjust, hypocrites, or disbelievers. Identify each source in the Arabic text.
3
Extract the three categories of heretical practices
In the latter part, he lists three specific types: (1) poems called 'janib al-Quran' preferred over the Quran, (2) poems claiming the shaykh is the creator (ittihad), (3) poems describing God with bodily attributes (tajsim). Write them down with evidence from the text.
4
Analyze the evidence Ibn Taymiyya uses
He points to fabricated hadith (the story of Umar) and false interpretations. How do these support his critique? Identify the logical link between the hadith and the categories.
5
Apply the framework to a hypothetical case
Consider a contemporary figure who claims esoteric knowledge and encourages followers to memorize his poetry over the Quran. Which category does this fall under? What would Ibn Taymiyya's critique be? Use his method to evaluate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المشايخ الصَّادقين من الكذب والمحال، أو يكون من كلامهم المتشابه الذي تأولوه على غير تأويله، أو يكون من غلطات بعض الشيوخ وزلاتهم، أو من ذنوب بعضهم وخطئهم، مثل كثير من البدع والفجور الذي يفعله بعضهم بتأويل سائغ أو بوجه غير سائغ، فيعفى عنه، أو يتوب، أو يكون منه ومن غيره حسنات يُغفر له بها، أو مصائب يكفّر عنه بها، أو يكون من كلام المتشبهين بأولياء الله من ذوي الزهادات والعبادات والمقالات، وليس هو من أولياء الله المتقين بل من الجاهلين الظالمين المعتدين أو المنافقين أو الكافرين. وهذا كثيرٌ مِلْءُ العالم، تجـد كـل قـوم يـدعـون مــن الاختصاص بالأسرار والحقائق ما لا يدَّعي المرسلون، وأن ذلك عند خواصهم، وأن ذلك لا يقابل إلا بالتسليم، ويحتجون لذلك بأحاديث موضوعة وتفسيرات باطلة، مثل قولهم عن عمر : إن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يتحدث هو وأبو بكر بحديث وكنتُ كالزنجي بينهما، فيجعلون عمر مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وصديقه كالزنجي، وهو حاضر يسمعُ الكلام، ثم يدَّعي أحدهم أنه عَلِمَ ذلك بما قُذِفَ في قلبه! ويدعي كل منهم أن ذلك هو ما يقوله من الزور والباطل. ولو ذكرتُ ما في هذا الباب من الأصناف لطال. فمنهم من يجعل للشيخ قصائد يسميها جنيب القرآن، ويكون وجده بها وفرحه بمضمونها أعظم من القرآن، ويكون فيها من الكذب والضلال أمور. ومنهم من يجعل له قصائد في الاتحاد، وأنه هو خالق جميع الخلق، وأنه خَلَق السموات والأرض، وأنه يُسْجَد له ويُعبد. ومنهم من يصفُ الربّ في قصائده بما نُقِل في الموضوعات من أصناف التمثيل والتكييف والتجسيم التي هي كذب مفترى وكفر صريح مثلُ مُواكَلته ومُشاريته ومُماشاته ومُعانقته ونزوله إلى الأرض وتعوده في بعض رياض الأرض ونحو ذلك.
The truthful shaykhs are [distinguished] from lying and impossibility, or it is from their ambiguous speech which they interpreted in other than its [proper] interpretation, or it is from mistakes of some shaykhs and their slips, or from sins of some of them and their errors, like many of the innovations and immorality which some of them do with an acceptable interpretation or in an unacceptable way, then he is forgiven, or repents, or there are from him and from others good deeds by which he is forgiven, or calamities by which he is expiated, or it is from the speech of those who imitate the friends of Allah among the people of asceticism, worship, and sayings, but he is not from the god-fearing friends of Allah, but rather from the ignorant, unjust, transgressors, hypocrites, or disbelievers. This is abundant, filling the world. You find every group claiming from specialization in secrets and realities what the messengers do not claim, and that that is with their elite, and that that is not met except with submission, and they argue for that with fabricated hadiths and false interpretations, like their saying about Umar: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) was conversing with Abu Bakr in a conversation, and I was like a black man between them.' So they make Umar with the Prophet and his friend like a black man, while he was present hearing the speech, then one of them claims that he knew that by what was cast into his heart! And each of them claims that that is what he says of falsehood and falsehood. And if I mentioned what is in this chapter of the categories, it would be lengthy. Among them are those who make for the shaykh poems which they call 'the companion of the Quran,' and his ecstasy with them and his joy in their content is greater than [with] the Quran, and they contain matters of lying and misguidance. Among them are those who make for him poems about union, that he is the creator of all creation, that he created the heavens and the earth, and that he is prostrated to and worshipped. Among them are those who describe the Lord in their poems with what was transmitted in the fabricated hadiths of kinds of comparison, qualification, and anthropomorphism which are fabricated lies and explicit disbelief, such as His eating with [someone], drinking with [someone], walking with [someone], embracing [someone], His descending to the earth, His returning to some gardens of the earth, and the like.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a critique by Ibn Taymiyya of various groups who falsely claim spiritual authority and esoteric knowledge. He begins by distinguishing the truthful shaykhs from the false ones, noting that false claims may arise from misinterpreting ambiguous speech, mistakes, sins, or from people who imitate the awliya but are actually ignorant, unjust, hypocrites, or disbelievers. He asserts that such pretensions are widespread: every group claims access to secrets and realities that even the messengers did not claim, demanding uncritical acceptance. They support their claims with fabricated hadiths, like the story that Umar was treated like a 'black man' (i.e., ignored) while the Prophet and Abu Bakr conversed, and that one of them 'knew' this through something cast into his heart. Ibn Taymiyya dismisses this as falsehood. He then lists three categories of such claimants: first, those who attribute to their shaykh poems that they call 'the companion of the Quran,' preferring them to the Quran; second, those who compose poems about union (ittihad), claiming the shaykh is the creator of all; third, those who describe God in their poems using fabricated anthropomorphic attributes like eating, drinking, walking, embracing, descending, and frequenting gardens. Ibn Taymiyya condemns all these as lies and clear disbelief. The passage shows his method of refuting heterodox doctrines by exposing their reliance on fabricated or misinterpreted texts.

Key Terms
الاتحاد (al-ittihād): In this passage, it refers to the heretical belief of union between the shaykh and the divine, to the extent that the shaykh is claimed to be the creator of all. [Note: In Sufi contexts, al-ittihad can mean mystical union; Ibn Taymiyya uses it here polemically to denote a pantheistic or incarnational heresy.]
التجسيم (al-tajsīm): Anthropomorphism: attributing a physical body or bodily characteristics to God, which Ibn Taymiyya considers kufr. [Note: The term is stable; it is a standard accusation in kalam against certain groups.]
الجنيب (al-janīb): Literally 'the led one' (a horse led alongside). Here it is used metaphorically for poems that are placed alongside the Quran, implying they are an alternative or supplement to it. [Note: In Sufi terminology, janib can refer to a disciple; here it is used by Ibn Taymiyya to criticize the elevation of such poems.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a category of false claimants criticized by Ibn Taymiyya?
A) Those who prefer poetry over the Quran
B) Those who claim their shaykh is the creator
C) Those who defend the use of analogical reasoning in theology
D) Those who describe God with bodily attributes

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's critique demonstrates that false spiritual authority is often supported by fabricated texts and heretical doctrines, and can be systematically identified by contrasting with the Quran and Sunnah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify which of the three categories (janib al-Quran, ittihad, tajsim) best fits the claim of a contemporary group that elevates a living scholar's poetry above the Quran. Justify your answer using Ibn Taymiyya's criteria.
?
Using Ibn Taymiyya's critique, evaluate the claim: 'The shaykh is the manifestation of God's attributes.' Would Ibn Taymiyya consider this a false claim? Which category does it fall under, and what evidence from the passage supports your conclusion?

Identifying Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Esoteric Knowledge Claims
Author criticizes false claimants to esoteric knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the types of false claimants to esoteric knowledge and reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's critique from the passage.

Core Idea
False claims of secret knowledge contradict the Quran and the explicit statements of the Prophet's family.

This passage from Ibn Taymiyya's Naqd al-Mantiq attacks those who claim hidden knowledge reserved for elites. He catalogs their fabrications and shows that they contradict authentic Islam. You will analyze his method of critique and learn to distinguish such falsehoods from genuine revealed knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of false claimants
Read the first part of the passage and list the three categories of people the author criticizes: those who prefer poetry over the Quran, those who claim union with God in a pantheistic way, and those who describe God with anthropomorphic fabrications.
The author groups them as examples of people who put their own compositions above revelation.
2
Extract the core claim of each group
For each category, note what they claim as 'hidden secrets' or 'preserved sciences'. See how they attribute these to elite status and demand concealment.
Their claims include that the shaykh is the Creator, and that God embodies human acts.
3
Find the specific historical counterexample
Locate the story of Ali ibn Abi Talib. The author uses this to show that the Prophet's own family denied having any hidden knowledge beyond the Quran. Write down the key point: Ali said 'No' when asked about extra-Quranic knowledge.
This is from Sahih hadith, making it a strong refutation.
4
Identify the author's epistemological grounding
Determine what authority the author appeals to: the Quran, authentic hadith, and the consensus of the Companions. He argues that these groups are the most lying because they attribute falsehoods to the Ahl al-Bayt.
The author uses a combination of textual evidence and historical testimony.
5
Summarize the critique's logical structure
The author sets up a general condemnation, provides examples, and then gives a specific refutation from history. Note that the critique is not just theological but also evidential.
This mirrors the typical critical method in Islamic scholarship: broad principle, concrete instance, and authoritative counterevidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ذكرتُ ما في هذا الباب من الأصناف لطال. فمنهم من يجعل للشيخ قصائد يسميها جنيب القرآن، ويكون وجده بها وفرحه بمضمونها أعظم من القرآن، ويكون فيها من الكذب والضلال أمور. ومنهم من يجعل له قصائد في الاتحاد، وأنه هو خالق جميع الخلق، وأنه خَلَق السموات والأرض، وأنه يُسْجَد له ويُعبد. ومنهم من يصفُ الربّ في قصائده بما نُقِل في الموضوعات من أصناف التمثيل والتكييف والتجسيم التي هي كذب مفترى وكفر صريح مثلُ مُواكَلته ومُشاريته ومُماشاته ومُعانقته ونزوله إلى الأرض وتعوده في بعض رياض الأرض ونحو ذلك. ويجعل كلّ منهم ذلك من الأسرار المخزونة والعلوم المصونة التي تكون لخواص أولياء الله المتقين. ومن أمثلة ذلك : أنك تجد عند الرافضة والمتشيّعة ومن أخذ عنهم من دعوى علوم الأسرار والحقائق التي يدَّعون أخذها عن أهل البيت ـ إمـا مـن العلوم الدينية وإما من علم الحوادث الكائنة ـ ما هو عندهم من أجل الأمور التي يجب التواصي بكتمانها والإيمان بما لا يُعْلَمُ حقيقته من ذلك. وجميعها كذب مختلقٌ وإفك مفترى، فإن هذه الطائفة من أكثر الطوائف كذبًا وادعاء للعلم المكتوم، ولهذا انتسبت إليهم الباطنية والقرامطة. وهؤلاء خرج أولهم في زمن أمير المؤمنين علي بن أبي طالب رَضَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، وصاروا يدَّعون أنه خُصَّ بأسرارٍ من العلوم والوصية، حتى كان يسأله عن ذلك خواص أصحابه فيخبرهم بانتفاء ذلك، ولما بلغه أن ذلـك قـد قيل كان يخطب الناس وينفي ذلك. وقد خرج أصحابُ الصَّحيح كلام عليّ هذا من غير وجه، مثل ما في الصحيح عن أبي جحيفة قال: سألتُ عليا : هل عندكم شيء ليس في القرآن؟ قال: لا.
And if I were to mention what is in this chapter regarding the types, it would be lengthy. Among them are those who compose for the shaykh poems they call 'the companion of the Qur'an,' and their ecstasy with them and joy in their content is greater than with the Qur'an, and in them there are matters of lying and misguidance. Among them are those who compose for him poems about union [with God], that he is the Creator of all creation, that he created the heavens and the earth, and that he is prostrated to and worshipped. Among them are those who describe the Lord in their poems with what has been transmitted among the fabricated [hadiths] of sorts of likening, qualification, and anthropomorphism, which are fabricated lies and clear disbelief, such as His eating, drinking, walking, embracing, descending to the earth, and frequenting some gardens of the earth, and the like. And each of them makes that from the hidden secrets and the preserved sciences which are for the elite of the pious friends of Allah. And among the examples of that: you find among the Rafidah and the Shia and those who took from them, claiming the sciences of secrets and realities which they claim to have taken from the Ahl al-Bayt — whether from the religious sciences or from knowledge of occurring events — that which is among the most important matters in their view that they must counsel each other to conceal and believe in without knowing its reality. And all of it is forged lying and fabricated slander, for this sect is among the most lying of sects and most given to claiming hidden knowledge, and for this reason the Batiniyyah and Qaramitah trace themselves back to them. And these [people], the first of them emerged in the time of the Commander of the Faithful Ali bin Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him, and they began to claim that he was distinguished with secrets of knowledge and a will, to the extent that his close companions would ask him about that, but he would inform them of the negation of that. And when it reached him that this had been said, he would deliver sermons to the people and deny it. And the compilers of authentic hadith have transmitted the words of Ali in more than one way, such as what is in the Sahih on the authority of Abu Juhaifah who said: I asked Ali: 'Do you have anything that is not in the Quran?' He said: 'No.'
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a critique of various groups that claim esoteric knowledge and secrets, preferring their own fabrications over the Qur'an and Sunnah. The author describes three types of claimants: those who extol their own poetry above the Qur'an; those who claim union with God and attribute divine acts to a human; and those who describe God in anthropomorphic terms found in fabricated hadiths. All of these groups consider their claims to be hidden secrets reserved for the elite pious. The author then gives a specific example from the Rafidah (a sect of Shia) and their followers, who claim secret sciences from the Ahl al-Bayt, including knowledge of future events. The author asserts that these claims are all lies and that the Rafidah are among the most lying of sects, which is why the Batiniyyah and Qaramitah (heretical groups) trace their origins to them. He then cites historical evidence from the time of Ali ibn Abi Talib, who explicitly denied having any special knowledge beyond the Qur'an, as recorded in authentic hadith. The passage serves to refute the notion of esoteric hidden knowledge that contradicts the revealed scripture and the statements of the Prophet's family.

Key Terms
جنيب القرآن
أسرار مخزونة
علوم مصونة
رافضة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Ali ibn Abi Talib say when asked if he had any knowledge not in the Quran?
A) He affirmed that he had secret knowledge from the Prophet.
B) He said no and denied having anything beyond the Quran.
C) He remained silent.
D) He said that knowledge is with the Imams after him.

Key Takeaway
Authentic Islamic knowledge is public and derived from the Quran and Sunnah; claims of secret esoteric knowledge are refuted by the very people to whom such knowledge is attributed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Using Ibn Taymiyya's method, write a short critique: state their claim, the counterevidence from authentic sources, and the flaw in their epistemology.
?
In the passage, the author uses the hadith of Abu Juhaifah to refute claims about Ali. Find another hadith from the Sahihayn where a Companion denies having special knowledge, and explain how it functions similarly as a refutation.

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Esoteric Knowledge Using Ali's Testimony
Author refutes esoteric knowledge claims with historical evidence from Ali's statements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's critique of esoteric knowledge claims and evaluate its internal consistency using Ali's statements.

Core Idea
Ali's own denials are the strongest refutation of claims of secret knowledge from him.

This passage from Ibn Taymiyya's Naqd al-Mantiq targets those who claim that the Ahl al-Bayt possessed hidden esoteric sciences. Instead of engaging in abstract logical argument, Ibn Taymiyya brings direct historical testimony from Ali ibn Abi Talib himself, who explicitly denied having any knowledge beyond the Quran and a practical scroll. By understanding how Ibn Taymiyya uses this evidence, you will learn a key method of critique: letting the authoritative figure refute the claims made in their name.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target claim
Locate the claims that Ibn Taymiyya is attacking: that the Rafidah and Shi'a assert they have secret sciences from the Ahl al-Bayt, including religious knowledge and knowledge of future events, which must be kept hidden.
Notice how Ibn Taymiyya characterizes these claims as 'lies and slander'.
2
Extract the historical evidence
Find the hadith quotations from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim where Ali denies having any revelation besides the Quran. In one, Ali says they have 'nothing except what is in the Quran, except an understanding... and what is in this scroll.' In another, he declares that anyone who claims they have a book besides the Quran has lied.
Pay attention to the multiple chains of transmission Ibn Taymiyya cites to establish authenticity.
3
Analyze the logical structure of the refutation
Ibn Taymiyya uses a form of argument from authority: the very person the claimants invoke (Ali) contradicts their claims. If Ali himself denied having such secrets, then the claimants are either lying or mistaken. This is a powerful refutation because it undermines the foundation of their authority.
This is not a syllogism but a direct witness testimony argument.
4
Evaluate the strength of the evidence
Consider why Ibn Taymiyya chose these specific hadith. They are from the most authentic sources (Bukhari and Muslim) and multiple narrations confirm Ali's denial. The scroll mentioned contains only practical rulings (blood-money, ransom, etc.), not esoteric secrets. This leaves no room for the claimants to reinterpret.
Ibn Taymiyya strengthens his case by emphasizing the authenticity of the chain: 'one of the most authentic chains on earth.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجعل كل‏ منهم ذلك من الأسرار المخزونة والعلوم المصونة التي تكون لخواص أولياء الله المتقين. ومن أمثلة ذلك : أنك تجد عند الرافضة والمتشيّعة ومن أخذ عنهم من دعوى علوم الأسرار والحقائق التي يدَّعون أخذها عن أهل البيت ـ إمـا مـن العلوم الدينية وإما من علم الحوادث الكائنة ـ ما هو عندهم من أجل الأمور التي يجب التواصي بكتمانها والإيمان بما لا يُعْلَمُ حقيقته من ذلك. وجميعها كذب مختلقٌ وإفك مفترى، فإن هذه الطائفة من أكثر الطوائف كذبًا وادعاء للعلم المكتوم، ولهذا انتسبت إليهم الباطنية والقرامطة. وهؤلاء خرج أولهم في زمن أمير المؤمنين علي بن أبي طالب رَضَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، وصاروا يدَّعون أنه خُصَّ بأسرارٍ من العلوم والوصية، حتى كان يسأله عن ذلك خواص أصحابه فيخبرهم بانتفاء ذلك، ولما بلغه أن ذلـك قـد قيل كان يخطب الناس وينفي ذلك. وقد خرج أصحابُ الصَّحيح كلام عليّ هذا من غير وجه، مثل ما في الصحيح عن أبي جحيفة قال: سألتُ عليا : هل عندكم شيء ليس في القرآن؟ فقال: لا، والذي فلق الحَبَّةَ وبَرَأ النَّسَمة، ما عندنا إلا ما في القرآن، إلا فهما يعطيه الله الرجل في كتابه وما في هذه الصحيفة. قلت: وما في الصحيفة ؟ قال : العَقْل، وفكاكُ الأسير، وأن لا يُقتل مسلم بكافر. ولفظ البخاري : هل عندكم شيء من الوحي إلا ما في كتاب الله؟ قال: لا، والذي فلق الحَبَّةَ وبَرَأ النَّسَمة، ما أعلمه إلا فهما يعطيه الله رجلًا في القرآن. وفي الصحيحين عن إبراهيم التّيمي عن أبيه [ عن علي] ـ وهذا من أصح إسنادٍ على وجه الأرض _ قال ما عندنا شي‏ _ قال: ما عندنا شيء إلا كتاب الله و هذه الصحيفة عن النبي : المدينةُ حَرَم ما بين عَيْرِ إلى ثور. وفي رواية لمسلم : خَطَبنا عليُّ بن أبي طالب فقال: من زعم أن عندنا كتابا نقرؤه إلا كتاب الله وما في هذه الصحيفة ـ قال: وصحيفته معلقة في قِرَاب سَيفه - فقد كَذَب فيها أسنانُ الإبل وأشياء من الجراحات، وفيها قال النبي : المدينةُ حَرَم... الحديث. وأما الكذبُ والأسرار التي يدعونها عن جعفر الصادق فمن أكثر
And each of them regards that as among the stored secrets and protected sciences that are for the special friends of Allah, the pious. Among examples of that is that you find among the Rafidah and the Shi'a and those who took from them, the claim of the sciences of secrets and realities which they claim to have taken from the Ahl al-Bayt—whether from religious sciences or from the knowledge of future events—that which is for them among the most important matters that must be kept secret and believed in without knowing its reality. And all of it is fabricated lies and false slander, for indeed this sect is among the most lying sects and claimant of hidden knowledge, and for this reason the Batiniyyah and Qaramitah affiliated with them. And these people, the first of them appeared in the time of the Commander of the Faithful Ali ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him, and they began to claim that he was singled out with secrets of knowledge and the bequest, to the extent that his close companions would ask him about that, and he would inform them of its non-existence. And when it reached him that this had been said, he would address the people and deny that. And the compilers of the Sahih have transmitted Ali's speech in multiple ways, such as in the Sahih from Abu Juhaifa who said: I asked Ali: 'Do you have anything that is not in the Quran?' He said: 'No, by Him who splits the seed and creates the soul, we have nothing except what is in the Quran, except an understanding that Allah gives a man in His Book and what is in this scroll.' I said: 'And what is in the scroll?' He said: 'The blood-money, and the ransom of the captive, and that a Muslim should not be killed for a disbeliever.' And the wording of al-Bukhari: 'Do you have anything from revelation except what is in the Book of Allah?' He said: 'No, by Him who splits the seed and creates the soul, I know of nothing except an understanding that Allah gives a man in the Quran.' And in the two Sahihs from Ibrahim al-Taymi from his father from Ali—and this is among the most authentic chains on the face of the earth—he said: 'We have nothing except the Book of Allah and this scroll from the Prophet: Madinah is sacred from 'Ayr to Thawr.' And in a narration of Muslim: Ali ibn Abi Talib addressed us and said: 'Whoever claims that we have a book that we read except the Book of Allah and what is in this scroll—and his scroll was hung in the sheath of his sword—has lied. In it are the ages of camels and matters of wounds.' And in it the Prophet said: 'Madinah is sacred...' the hadith. And as for the lies and secrets which they claim from Ja'far al-Sadiq, they are among the greatest.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation from Ibn Taymiyya against those who claim esoteric knowledge, particularly the Rafidah and Shi'a who assert that they possess hidden sciences from the Ahl al-Bayt. The author begins by characterizing these claims as lies and slander. He then provides historical evidence from the time of Ali ibn Abi Talib, showing that the first proponents of such ideas emerged during Ali's caliphate, claiming that Ali was given special secrets. But Ali himself, when asked by his close companions, denied having any knowledge beyond the Quran and a specific scroll. Ibn Taymiyya cites multiple authenticated hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim to support this. In one hadith, Abu Juhaifa asks Ali directly if they have anything not in the Quran; Ali answers no, except for an understanding Allah grants and the scroll containing legal rulings about blood-money and ransom. Another narration has Ali publicly declaring that anyone who claims they have a book besides the Quran has lied. The scroll only contained specific practical rulings, not hidden esoteric truths. The author thus dismantles the foundation of esoteric knowledge claims by using Ali's own words. This passage exemplifies Ibn Taymiyya's method of critiquing rival groups through scriptural and historical evidence.

Authentic Source: What Ali's Scroll Contained
Author critiques claims of secret books by citing authentic hadiths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the contents of Ali's scroll and explain why it does not constitute a book of continuous revelation.

Core Idea
The only authoritative sources are Quran and authentic Sunnah; Ali's scroll was a legal document, not a book of secrets.

This lesson uses a critical passage from the author to distinguish between authentic transmission and fabricated books. The hadith from Ali ibn Abi Talib clearly states what the companions possessed beyond the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Locate the hadith of Ali in the passage
Find the narration where Ali denies having any book except the Quran and a scroll. Note the exact wording.
The hadith appears in both Bukhari and Muslim.
2
Extract the scroll's contents
List the three items mentioned: blood money, ransom of captive, and that a Muslim is not killed for a disbeliever.
3
Understand the nature of the scroll
The scroll (sahifa) contained specific legal rulings, not continuous revelation. The author uses this to show that no companion claimed a secret book.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القرآن؟ فقال: لا، والذي فلق الحَبَّةَ وبَرَأ النَّسَمة، ما عندنا إلا ما في القرآن، إلا فهما يعطيه الله الرجل في كتابه وما في هذه الصحيفة. قلت: وما في الصحيفة؟ قال: العَقْل، وفكاكُ الأسير، وأن لا يُقتل مسلم بكافر. ولفظ البخاري: هل عندكم شيء من الوحي إلا ما في كتاب الله؟ قال: لا، والذي فلق الحَبَّةَ وبَرَأ النَّسَمة، ما أعلمه إلا فهما يعطيه الله رجلًا في القرآن. وفي الصحيحين عن إبراهيم التّيمي عن أبيه عن علي قال: ما عندنا شيء إلا كتاب الله و هذه الصحيفة عن النبي: المدينةُ حَرَم ما بين عَيْرِ إلى ثور. وفي رواية لمسلم: خَطَبنا عليُّ بن أبي طالب فقال: من زعم أن عندنا كتابا نقرؤه إلا كتاب الله وما في هذه الصحيفة ـ قال: وصحيفته معلقة في قِرَاب سَيفه - فقد كَذَب فيها أسنانُ الإبل وأشياء من الجراحات، وفيها قال النبي: المدينةُ حَرَم... الحديث. وأما الكذبُ والأسرار التي يدعونها عن جعفر الصادق فمن أكثر الأشياء، حتى يقال: ما كُذِبَ على أحدٍ ما كُذِبَ على جعفر رَضَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ. ومن هذه الأمور المضافة: كتاب «الجَفْر» الذي يدَّعون أنه كتب فيه الحوادث، والجَفْر: ولد الماعز، يزعمون أنه كتب ذلك في جِلْدِه. وكذلك كتاب «البطاقة» الذي يدَّعيه ابن أحلى ونحوه من
The Quran? He said: No, by Him who splits the seed and creates the soul, we have nothing except what is in the Quran, except understanding that God gives a man in His Book and what is in this scroll. I said: And what is in the scroll? He said: The blood money, the ransom of the captive, and that a Muslim is not killed for a disbeliever. And the wording of al-Bukhari: Do you have anything of revelation except what is in the Book of God? He said: No, by Him who splits the seed and creates the soul, I know nothing except understanding that God gives a man in the Quran. And in the two Sahihs, from Ibrahim al-Taymi from his father from Ali: He said: We have nothing except the Book of God and this scroll from the Prophet: Medina is a sanctuary between 'Ayr and Thawr. And in a narration of Muslim: Ali ibn Abi Talib addressed us and said: Whoever claims that we have a book we read except the Book of God and what is in this scroll—he said: and his scroll was hanging in the sheath of his sword—has lied, in it are the teeth of camels and things from wounds, and in it the Prophet said: Medina is a sanctuary... the hadith. And as for the lies and secrets they claim from Ja'far al-Sadiq, it is among the greatest things, so much so that it is said: No one has been lied about as much as Ja'far, may God be pleased with him. And among these added things: the book 'al-Jafr' which they claim contains events, and al-Jafr is a young goat; they claim that it was written on its skin. And likewise the book 'al-Bitaqa' which Ibn Ahla and similar people claim.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a critique by the author of claims that the early Muslims possessed secret books of knowledge beyond the Quran. The author begins by citing several authentic hadiths from the companions, particularly Ali ibn Abi Talib, who explicitly denies having any book other than the Quran and a small scroll containing specific rulings: blood money, ransom of captives, and the prohibition of killing a Muslim for a disbeliever. Al-Bukhari's narration emphasizes that revelation is only in the Quran, with the exception of understanding granted by God. The author then moves to the more exaggerated claims attributed to Ja'far al-Sadiq, noting that no one has been lied about more than him. Among these fabrications are the books 'al-Jafr' (supposedly written on a goat's skin) and 'al-Bitaqa', claimed by Ibn Ahla and others. The author implies that these are baseless and contrary to the practice of the early Muslims.

الجفر
البطاقة

Fabricated Books: Rejecting al-Jafr and al-Bitaqa
Author critiques claims of secret books like al-Jafr and al-Bitaqa attributed to Ja'far al-Sadiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the fabricated books al-Jafr and al-Bitaqa and explain the author's critique of them.

Core Idea
No one has been more lied about than Ja'far al-Sadiq; claims of secret books are baseless.

The author expands from the authentic hadith to critique widespread fabrications attributed to Ja'far al-Sadiq. These include books claiming to contain future events, such as al-Jafr and al-Bitaqa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fabricated books
Find where the author mentions al-Jafr and al-Bitaqa. Note the description: al-Jafr is written on a goat's skin, al-Bitaqa is claimed by Ibn Ahla.
2
Understand the author's critique
The author states that no one has been lied about as much as Ja'far al-Sadiq, implying these books are among those lies.
3
Connect to the earlier hadith
The author uses the authentic testimony of Ali to undermine the credibility of these later fabrications. If the companions had no secret books, later claims are false.

القرآن؟ فقال: لا، والذي فلق الحَبَّةَ وبَرَأ النَّسَمة، ما عندنا إلا ما في القرآن، إلا فهما يعطيه الله الرجل في كتابه وما في هذه الصحيفة. قلت: وما في الصحيفة؟ قال: العَقْل، وفكاكُ الأسير، وأن لا يُقتل مسلم بكافر. ولفظ البخاري: هل عندكم شيء من الوحي إلا ما في كتاب الله؟ قال: لا، والذي فلق الحَبَّةَ وبَرَأ النَّسَمة، ما أعلمه إلا فهما يعطيه الله رجلًا في القرآن. وفي الصحيحين عن إبراهيم التّيمي عن أبيه عن علي قال: ما عندنا شيء إلا كتاب الله و هذه الصحيفة عن النبي: المدينةُ حَرَم ما بين عَيْرِ إلى ثور. وفي رواية لمسلم: خَطَبنا عليُّ بن أبي طالب فقال: من زعم أن عندنا كتابا نقرؤه إلا كتاب الله وما في هذه الصحيفة ـ قال: وصحيفته معلقة في قِرَاب سَيفه - فقد كَذَب فيها أسنانُ الإبل وأشياء من الجراحات، وفيها قال النبي: المدينةُ حَرَم... الحديث. وأما الكذبُ والأسرار التي يدعونها عن جعفر الصادق فمن أكثر الأشياء، حتى يقال: ما كُذِبَ على أحدٍ ما كُذِبَ على جعفر رَضَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ. ومن هذه الأمور المضافة: كتاب «الجَفْر» الذي يدَّعون أنه كتب فيه الحوادث، والجَفْر: ولد الماعز، يزعمون أنه كتب ذلك في جِلْدِه. وكذلك كتاب «البطاقة» الذي يدَّعيه ابن أحلى ونحوه من
The Quran? He said: No, by Him who splits the seed and creates the soul, we have nothing except what is in the Quran, except understanding that God gives a man in His Book and what is in this scroll. I said: And what is in the scroll? He said: The blood money, the ransom of the captive, and that a Muslim is not killed for a disbeliever. And the wording of al-Bukhari: Do you have anything of revelation except what is in the Book of God? He said: No, by Him who splits the seed and creates the soul, I know nothing except understanding that God gives a man in the Quran. And in the two Sahihs, from Ibrahim al-Taymi from his father from Ali: He said: We have nothing except the Book of God and this scroll from the Prophet: Medina is a sanctuary between 'Ayr and Thawr. And in a narration of Muslim: Ali ibn Abi Talib addressed us and said: Whoever claims that we have a book we read except the Book of God and what is in this scroll—he said: and his scroll was hanging in the sheath of his sword—has lied, in it are the teeth of camels and things from wounds, and in it the Prophet said: Medina is a sanctuary... the hadith. And as for the lies and secrets they claim from Ja'far al-Sadiq, it is among the greatest things, so much so that it is said: No one has been lied about as much as Ja'far, may God be pleased with him. And among these added things: the book 'al-Jafr' which they claim contains events, and al-Jafr is a young goat; they claim that it was written on its skin. And likewise the book 'al-Bitaqa' which Ibn Ahla and similar people claim.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a critique by the author of claims that the early Muslims possessed secret books of knowledge beyond the Quran. The author begins by citing several authentic hadiths from the companions, particularly Ali ibn Abi Talib, who explicitly denies having any book other than the Quran and a small scroll containing specific rulings: blood money, ransom of captives, and the prohibition of killing a Muslim for a disbeliever. Al-Bukhari's narration emphasizes that revelation is only in the Quran, with the exception of understanding granted by God. The author then moves to the more exaggerated claims attributed to Ja'far al-Sadiq, noting that no one has been lied about more than him. Among these fabrications are the books 'al-Jafr' (supposedly written on a goat's skin) and 'al-Bitaqa', claimed by Ibn Ahla and others. The author implies that these are baseless and contrary to the practice of the early Muslims.

البطاقة

A) They contradict the Quran.

C) The books were lost.
D) Ibn Ahla admitted they were false.

Key Takeaway
Al-Jafr and al-Bitaqa are fabrications; the author rejects them based on the absence of such books among the companions and the prevalence of lies about Ja'far al-Sadiq.

Ibn Taymiyya's Exposure of Forged Books Attributed to Jafar al-Sadiq
Ibn Taymiyya enumerates falsely attributed books and warns against them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four books Ibn Taymiyya lists as falsely attributed to Jafar al-Sadiq and explain the basis for his critique.

Core Idea
The most lied-about scholar in Islamic history: Jafar al-Sadiq.

Ibn Taymiyya dedicates a passage to exposing books falsely ascribed to the revered scholar Jafar al-Sadiq. He notes that no one has been lied about more than him. This lesson unpacks his list of fabricated works and the scholarly warnings against them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opening claim
Ibn Taymiyya states that Jafar al-Sadiq has been lied about more than anyone else. This sets the tone for exposing the scale of forgery.
The phrase 'ما كُذِبَ على أحدٍ ما كُذِبَ على جعفر' is a strong indictment.
2
List the four books
Extract the names: al-Jafr, al-Bitaqa, al-Jadwal, al-Haft. Note what each is claimed to contain according to Ibn Taymiyya.
al-Jafr is particularly notable: events written on the skin of a young goat.
3
Note the groups making these claims
Ibn Taymiyya mentions 'they' (the claimants) and specifically 'Ibn Ahla' for al-Bitaqa. Also the Maghrebis. Recognize that these are sectarian groups like Ismailis.
The critic identifies the source of the fraud.
4
Recognize the scholarly refutations
Ibn Taymiyya mentions that a book and long poem were written in refutation, and scholars like Abu Hayyan and Zarruq warned against these works.
This shows that the critique is not isolated but part of a scholarly consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأشياء، حتى يقال : ما كُذِبَ على أحدٍ ما كُذِبَ على جعفر رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ. ومن هذه الأمور المضافة: كتاب «الجَفْر» الذي يدَّعون أنه كتب فيه الحوادث، والجَفْر : ولد الماعز، يزعمون أنه كتب ذلك في جِلْدِه. وكذلك كتاب «البطاقة» الذي يدَّعيه ابن أحلى ونحوه من المغاربة. ومثل كتاب «الجدول» في الهلال، و«الهَفت» عن جعفر، وكثير من تفسير القرآن، وغيره. وفي الردّ عليه كتاب ورجز طويل، وحذَّر منه أبو حيان في «البحر المحيط» وزروق في كتابيه «قواعد التصوف» و«عدة المريد الصادق».
Things, so that it is said: No one has been lied about as much as Jafar, may Allah be pleased with him. And from these added matters: The book 'al-Jafr' which they claim he wrote events in, and al-Jafr is the young goat; they claim he wrote that on its skin. And likewise the book 'al-Bitaqa' which Ibn Ahla claims, and similar ones from the Maghrebis. And like the book 'al-Jadwal' concerning the crescent, and 'al-Haft' from Jafar, and much of the interpretation of the Quran, and others. And in refutation of it there is a long book and poem, and Abu Hayyan warned from it in 'al-Bahr al-Muhit' and Zarruq in his two books 'Qawa'id al-Tasawwuf' and 'Uddat al-Murid al-Sadiq'.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a critical enumeration by Ibn Taymiyya of books falsely attributed to the revered scholar Jafar al-Sadiq. He begins by noting the extreme prevalence of lies about Jafar, more than anyone else. Then he lists specific books from 'the added matters' (al-umur al-mudafa), i.e., fabricated works. The first is 'al-Jafr', which they claim contains predictions written on the skin of a young goat. Second is 'al-Bitaqa', claimed by Ibn Ahla, associated with Maghrebi mystics. Third is 'al-Jadwal' concerning crescent sighting, and fourth is 'al-Haft' from Jafar, along with many Quranic interpretations attributed to him. Ibn Taymiyya then mentions that there is a refutation of this book (likely 'al-Haft') consisting of a long book and poem, and that scholars like Abu Hayyan and Zarruq warned against it. The purpose is to expose the falsehood of these attributions, protecting the integrity of Islamic knowledge. The passage is concise but powerful in its condemnation of fabricated traditions.

البطاقة
الجدول
الهَفت

Ibn Taymiyya Exposes False Books: al-Jadwal, al-Haft, and Tafsir Attributions
Ibn Taymiyya lists and critiques books falsely attributed to Ja'far al-Sadiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify three types of works falsely attributed to Ja'far al-Sadiq (al-Jadwal, al-Haft, and tafsir) and explain Ibn Taymiyya's grounds for rejecting them based on scholarly warnings and content analysis.

Core Idea
False attributions to revered figures poison the tradition; Ibn Taymiyya exposes them with historical and scholarly evidence.

Ibn Taymiyya begins his critique by listing several books that are wrongly ascribed to Ja'far al-Sadiq. These include a numerical work on crescent calculation, an Ismaili text, and much of the Quran commentary. He points out that scholars like Abu Hayyan and Zarruq have already warned against them. By examining his method, we learn how critical scholarship protects the integrity of Islamic heritage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claimed sources
List the three types of works Ibn Taymiyya mentions as falsely attributed to Ja'far al-Sadiq: 'al-Jadwal' (a book on crescent calculation), 'al-Haft' (an Ismaili book), and 'much of the commentary on the Quran'.
These are not exhaustive; they are examples of false attributions.
2
Examine Ibn Taymiyya's evidence
What reasons does Ibn Taymiyya give for rejecting these attributions? He notes that 'al-Jadwal' has been refuted in a long book and poem, and that scholars Abu Hayyan and Zarruq have warned against it. For 'al-Haft' and the tafsir, the implication is that they contain ideas inconsistent with Ja'far's true teachings.
Ibn Taymiyya relies on both internal (content) and external (scholarly consensus) evidence.
3
Understand the doctrinal stakes
Why does Ibn Taymiyya consider it important to expose these forgeries? Because false attributions can lead to doctrinal corruption: people may adopt beliefs or practices based on fabricated texts, thinking they come from an authoritative Imām.
This is a common concern in Islamic disciplines like hadith criticism (al-jarh wa al-ta'dil).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومثل كتاب «الجدول» في الهلال، و«الهَفت» عن جعفر، وكثير من تفسير القرآن، وغيره. في الردّ عليه كتاب ورجز طويل، وحذَّر منه أبو حيان في «البحر المحيط» وزروق في كتابيه «قواعد التصوف» و «عدة المريد الصادق». ومثل كتاب رسائل إخوان الصفا الذي صنفه جماعة في دولة بني بوَيْه ببغداد وكانوا من الصابئة المتفلسفة المتحنّفة، جمعوا بزعمهم بين دين الصابئة المبدلين وبين الحَنِيفيَّة، وأتوا بكلام المتفلسفة وبأشياء من الشريعة، وفيه من الكفر والجهل شيء كثير، ومع هذا فطائفة من الناس من بعض أكابر قضاة النواحي يزعم أنه من كلام جعفر الصادق وهذا قول زنديق وتشنيع جاهل. ومثل ما يذكره بعض العامة من ملاحِم أبن عقب، ويزعمون أنه
And like the book 'al-Jadwal' on the crescent, and 'al-Haft' from Ja'far, and much of the commentary on the Quran, and others. In refutation of it there is a long book and poem, and Abu Hayyan warned against it in 'al-Bahr al-Muhit' and Zarruq in his two books 'Qawa'id al-Tasawwuf' and 'Uddat al-Murid al-Sadiq'. And like the book 'Rasa'il Ikhwan al-Safa', which a group authored in the state of Bani Buwayh in Baghdad, and they were from the Sabians, the philosophizing, the hanif-seeking; they claimed to combine the religion of the altered Sabians with Hanifiyya, and they brought the speech of the philosophers and some things from the Sharia, and in it there is much disbelief and ignorance. Yet a group of people from some senior judges of the regions claim that it is the speech of Ja'far al-Sadiq, and this is a heretical statement and the ignorance of an ignorant person. And like what some common people mention of the 'Malahim' of Ibn 'Aqab, claiming that...
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a critical enumeration by Ibn Taymiyya of books falsely attributed to the revered figure Ja'far al-Sadiq. The author's aim is to expose these fabrications and warn against them. He first mentions 'al-Jadwal', a work on crescent calculation based solely on numbers without sighting, claimed by some Ismailis and Shi'a to have been given to them by Ja'far. Ibn Taymiyya notes that it has been refuted, and that scholars like Abu Hayyan and Zarruq have warned against it. Next, he discusses 'al-Haft', an Ismaili book allegedly transmitted by Mufaddal ibn 'Umar al-Ju'fi from Ja'far, but which the Twelver Shi'a disavow. He also refers to much of the Quran commentary attributed to Ja'far, particularly the sayings collected by al-Sulami in 'Haqa'iq al-Tafsir', which Ibn Taymiyya considers unreliable. The second example is the famous 'Rasa'il Ikhwan al-Safa' (Epistles of the Brethren of Purity). Ibn Taymiyya explains that these were composed by a group of Sabian philosophers in the Buyid era, attempting to blend Sabianism with Islam. He states that the work contains much disbelief and ignorance, yet some judges wrongly attribute it to Ja'far al-Sadiq. Ibn Taymiyya calls this a heretical and ignorant claim, as the epistles were written more than two hundred years after Ja'far's death. The third example, cut off in the OCR, concerns the 'Malahim' (apocalyptic predictions) of Ibn 'Aqab, which common people claim. Throughout, Ibn Taymiyya is meticulously correcting historical and doctrinal errors, using his extensive knowledge of Islamic history and theology to safeguard the integrity of the tradition.

Key Terms
جدول
هفت
البحر المحيط
قواعد التصوف
عدة المريد الصادق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya employs scholarly consensus and refutation literature to expose forged attributions, a method essential for preserving the integrity of Islamic teachings.

Ibn Taymiyya Exposes the False Attribution of Ikhwan al-Safa to Ja'far al-Sadiq
Ibn Taymiyya critiques the false attribution of Rasa'il Ikhwan al-Safa to Ja'far al-Sadiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Ibn Taymiyya rejects the attribution of the 'Rasa'il Ikhwan al-Safa' to Ja'far al-Sadiq, citing historical evidence about its true authorship and the dangers of such false attribution.

Core Idea
The Epistles of Ikhwan al-Safa are a Sabian philosophical work, not the words of Ja'far al-Sadiq.

Ibn Taymiyya now turns to one of the most famous forgeries: the 'Rasa'il Ikhwan al-Safa' (Epistles of the Brethren of Purity). He reveals that these epistles were composed by a group of Sabian philosophers in the Buyid era, not by Imām Ja'far. He also warns that some judges actually claim they are from Ja'far, calling this a heretical and ignorant statement. In this lesson, we dissect his historical argument and understand why this attribution is so problematic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work in question
What is 'Rasa'il Ikhwan al-Safa'? It is a collection of philosophical epistles that aim to reconcile Greek philosophy with religion. Ibn Taymiyya says it was authored by a group of Sabian philosophers in Baghdad during the Buyid dynasty.
The Buyid dynasty ruled from the 10th to 11th centuries, long after Ja'far al-Sadiq (d. 765).
2
Analyze Ibn Taymiyya's historical argument
Ibn Taymiyya provides three key pieces of evidence: (1) the work was authored by a group, not an individual; (2) they were Sabian philosophers who attempted to blend Sabianism with Hanifiyya (a pre-Islamic monotheism); (3) they lived in the Buyid period, more than 200 years after Ja'far's death. Therefore, it cannot be from Ja'far.
The Sabians are often identified with Hermetic or star-worshipping groups; Ibn Taymiyya frequently critiques them.
3
Evaluate the impact of the false attribution
Why does this false attribution matter? Ibn Taymiyya states that the epistles contain 'much disbelief and ignorance'. If accepted as Ja'far's words, they would introduce philosophical ideas incompatible with true Islam. He also notes that some senior judges claim this attribution, which makes the error more dangerous due to their authority.
Ibn Taymiyya calls this 'a heretical statement and the ignorance of an ignorant person', emphasizing the severity.

And like the book 'al-Jadwal' on the crescent, and 'al-Haft' from Ja'far, and much of the commentary on the Quran, and others. Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of False Attributions: Ikhwan al-Safa and Malahim
Ibn Taymiyya critiques false claims linking later texts to early Islamic figures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Taymiyya's method for refuting false historical attributions and apply it to similar cases in Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya exposes how texts are falsely attributed to early authorities, undermining their credibility.

Ibn Taymiyya was deeply concerned with the authenticity of texts attributed to early Islamic figures. In this passage from Naqd al-Mantiq, he takes aim at two fraudulent attributions: the Epistles of Ikhwan al-Safa being credited to Imam Ja'far al-Sadiq, and the apocalyptic malahim poems being linked to a teacher of Hasan and Husayn. He shows how historical anachronism and the identity of the authors reveal these claims as fabrications. This lesson will equip you with the tools to critically assess such attributions in your own studies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Read the passage and pinpoint the two specific false attributions Ibn Taymiyya addresses: the Ikhwan al-Safa epistles attributed to Ja'far al-Sadiq, and the malahim of Ibn 'Uqbah attributed to a teacher of Hasan and Husayn.
2
Determine the true origin
For each case, extract what Ibn Taymiyya says is the actual origin—who wrote it, when, and why. For Ikhwan al-Safa: a group of Sabian philosophers during the Buyid period. For malahim: ignorant people during the time of Nur al-Din.
3
Examine the evidence
Note the specific reasons Ibn Taymiyya gives for rejecting the attribution: historical anachronism (Ja'far al-Sadiq lived two centuries before the Buyids; Ibn 'Uqbah could not have taught Hasan and Husayn), content analysis (the epistles contain disbelief; the poems are corrupt), and consensus of scholars (the malahim are unknown to scholars).
4
Assess the severity
Ibn Taymiyya uses strong terms: 'zindiq' (heretic) and 'jahil' (ignorant) for those who make these claims. Understand that misattributions are not minor errors but serious offenses that can lead to religious distortion.
5
Generalize the principle
Ibn Taymiyya concludes that such fabrications are widespread and warns that even in his time, judges and shaykhs produce new false attributions. The principle: always verify the provenance of texts before accepting them as authoritative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومثل كتاب رسائل إخوان الصفا الذي صنفه جماعة في دولة بني بوَيْه ببغداد وكانوا من الصابئة المتفلسفة المتحنّفة، جمعوا بزعمهم بين دين الصابئة المبدلين وبين الحَنِيفيَّة، وأتوا بكلام المتفلسفة وبأشياء من الشريعة، وفيه من الكفر والجهل شيء كثير، ومع هذا فطائفة من الناس من بعض أكابر قضاة النواحي يزعم أنه من كلام جعفر الصادق وهذا قول زنديق وتشنيع جاهل. ومثل ما يذكره بعض العامة من ملاحِم ابن عقب، ويزعمون أنه كان معلما للحسن والحسين. وهذا شيء لم يكن في الوجود باتفاق أهل العلم، وملاحمه إنما صنفها بعض الجهال في دولة نور الدين ونحوها، وهو شعرٌ فاسد نظَمَه جاهل. وكذلك عامةُ هذه الملاحم المرويَّة بالنظم ونحوه عامتها من الأكاذيب، وقد أُحدِثَ في زماننا من القضاة والمشايخ غير واحدة منها، وقرّرتُ بعض
And like the book of the Epistles of the Ikhwan al-Safa, which a group authored during the state of the Banu Buwayh in Baghdad, and they were from the Sabian philosophizing Hanafites, who claimed to combine between the religion of the altered Sabians and the Hanafiyyah, and they brought the speech of the philosophers and some things from the Sharia, and in it is much disbelief and ignorance. Yet despite this, a group of people from some of the senior judges of the regions claim that it is from the speech of Ja'far al-Sadiq, and this is a zindiq statement and the rebuke of an ignorant person. And like what some common people mention from the malahim of Ibn 'Uqbah, and they claim that he was a teacher of al-Hasan and al-Husayn. This is something that did not exist by the agreement of the people of knowledge, and his malahim were only authored by some ignorant people in the state of Nur al-Din and the like, and it is corrupt poetry that an ignorant person composed. And likewise, the generality of these malahim transmitted in poetry and the like are mostly lies, and in our time there have been produced by judges and shaykhs not one of them, and I have established some...
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a critique by Ibn Taymiyya of false attributions of texts to early Islamic figures. He gives two examples. First, the Epistles of the Ikhwan al-Safa were written by a group of Sabian philosophers during the Buyid period in Baghdad. They claimed to combine Sabian and Hanafi beliefs but mixed philosophy with some Sharia. Despite its content of disbelief and ignorance, some prominent judges claim it is from Imam Ja'far al-Sadiq, who lived two centuries earlier. Ibn Taymiyya calls such a claim 'zindiq' (heretical) and the utterance of an ignorant person. Second, the malahim (apocalyptic poems) attributed to Ibn 'Uqbah are claimed by some common people to have been a teacher of Hasan and Husayn, the grandsons of the Prophet. Ibn Taymiyya states this is historically impossible by consensus of scholars; these poems were fabricated by ignorant people during the time of Nur al-Din (12th century). He dismisses them as corrupt poetry. He then generalizes that all such malahim transmitted in poetry are mostly lies, and in his own time, new fabrications have been produced by judges and shaykhs. The passage ends mid-sentence, indicating he began to detail some of these.

Key Terms
إخوان الصفا
ملاحم
زنديق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) A group of Sabian philosophers during the Buyid period
C) The judges of the regions
D) Nur al-Din

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya demonstrates that false attributions can be refuted by historical evidence and scholarly consensus, protecting the integrity of Islamic knowledge.

Find a contemporary claim that a certain fatwa or book is from an early imam (e.g., attributing a work to Imam Abu Hanifa). Use Ibn Taymiyya's method to assess its authenticity: check the earliest manuscript evidence, historical context, and scholarly consensus.

Write a brief analysis of why the attribution of the Epistles of Ikhwan al-Safa to Ja'far al-Sadiq is anachronistic, using Ibn Taymiyya's points.

Distinguishing Lawful Optimism from Prohibited Divination
Ibn Taymiyya distinguishes prohibited divination from lawful optimism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between prohibited divination (istisqam bil-azlam) and lawful optimism (fa'l) using Ibn Taymiyya's criteria of tawakkul and object manipulation.

Core Idea
The key difference is trust in Allah versus reliance on manipulated objects.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya exposes how diviners lie by using celestial signs or physical objects to claim knowledge of the unseen. In contrast, the Prophet's optimism (fa'l) is based on hearing good words while trusting Allah. Understanding this distinction is crucial to avoid falling into shirk while practicing permissible optimism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of divination
Ibn Taymiyya mentions celestial signs (stars, thunder, etc.) and man-made methods (sand, pebbles, lotteries). Locate these in the Arabic text.
2
Extract the defining characteristic of prohibited divination
Note that all prohibited methods involve altering physical objects to extract unknown knowledge. This is akin to istisqam bil-azlam.
3
Contrast with lawful optimism (fa'l)
Fa'l is when one goes out trusting in Allah and hears a good word. It strengthens tawakkul. There is no manipulation of objects.
4
Apply the principle
Determine whether a practice like reading coffee grounds is closer to prohibited divination or lawful optimism. Justify using the criteria.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هؤلاء (۱) على ذلك بعد أن أدعى قِدَمها، وقلت: بل أنتَ صنفتها، فأقر أنه صنّفها ولبسها على بعض ملوك المسلمين لما كان المسلمون محاصري عكا، وكذلك غيره من القضاة وغيرهم لبسوا على غير هذا الملك.
وباب الكذب في الحوادث الكونيّة أكثرُ منه في الأمور الدينية؛ لأن تشوف الذين يُغَلَّبون الدنيا على الدين إلى ذلك أكثر، وإن كان لأهل الدين إلى ذلك تشرُّفٌ لكن تشوفهم إلى الدين أقوى، وأولئك ليس لهم من الفرقان بين الحق والباطل ومن النور (۲) ما لأهل الدين، فلهذا كثر الكذابون في ذلك ونَفَقَ منه شيءٌ كثير، وأكلت به أموال عظيمة بالباطل، وقتلت به نفوس كثيرة من المتشوفة إلى الملك ونحوها.
ولهذا ينوعون طرق الكذب في ذلك، ويَعْتَمِدون الكذب فيه تارةً بالإحالة على الحركات والأشكال الجسمانية الإلهية (۳) من حركات الأفلاك والكواكب والشُّهب والرعود والبروق والرياح وغير ذلك (٤). وتارةً بما يُحْدِثُونه (٥) هم من الحركات والأشكال، كالرمل (٦) والحصى والشعير والقُرعة بأبجد (۱) ونحو ذلك مما هو من جنس الاستقسام بالأزلام، فإنهم يطلبون علم الحوادث بما يفعلونه من الاستقسام بها، سواء كانت قداحًا أو حصى أو غير ذلك مما ذكره أهل العلم بالتفسير (٢) . فكل ما يُحدِثه الإنسان بحركة من تغيير شيء من الأجسام ليستخرج به ما يجهله (۳) فهو من هذا الجنس، بخلاف الفأل الشرعي، وهو الذي كان يُعْجِبُ النبي ، وهو أن يخرج متوكلا على الله، فيسمع الكلمة الطيبة وكان يُعْجِبُه الفأل، ويكره الطَّيَرة» (٤) ؛ لأن الفأل تقوية لما فعله بإذن الله والتوكَّل عليه، والطَّيَرةُ معارضة لذلك، فكره للإنسان (٥) أن يتطيَّر، وإنما تضرُّ الطيرةُ مَن تطيَّر لأنه ضرَّ نفسَه، فأما المتوكل على الله فلا.
وليس المقصود ذكر هذه الأمور وسبب إصابتها تارةً وخطئها تارات وإنما الغرض أنهم يتعمَّدون (٦) فيها كذبًا كثيرًا من غير أن تكون دلت على
These (1) are upon that after he claimed its antiquity, and I said: Rather you composed it, so he admitted that he composed it and dressed it upon some of the Muslim kings when the Muslims were besieging Acre, and likewise other judges and others dressed upon other than this king. And the domain of lying in worldly events is greater than in religious matters; because the aspiration of those who give precedence to the world over religion towards that is greater, and even if the people of religion have aspiration towards that, their aspiration towards religion is stronger, and those do not have from the criterion between truth and falsehood and from the light (2) what the people of religion have, so for this reason the liars became numerous in that and much of it became current, and by it great wealth was consumed unjustly, and many souls of those aspiring to kingship and the like were killed. And for this reason they diversify the ways of lying in that, and they rely on lying in it sometimes by attribution to the divine celestial motions and shapes (3) from the motions of the orbs, planets, meteors, thunders, lightnings, winds, and other things (4). And sometimes by what they themselves produce (5) of motions and shapes, like sand (6), pebbles, barley, and lottery by abjad (1) and the like, which are of the genus of divination by arrows, for they seek knowledge of events by what they do of divination with them, whether they were arrows or pebbles or other things mentioned by the people of knowledge of tafsir (2). So everything that a human produces by a motion of changing something from bodies to extract what he is ignorant of (3) is of this genus, contrary to the lawful optimism, which the Prophet used to like, and it is that he goes out trusting in Allah and hears a good word, and he used to like optimism and dislike pessimism (4); because optimism strengthens what he does by Allah's permission and trust in Him, and pessimism opposes that, so it is disliked for a person (5) to be pessimistic, and indeed pessimism harms only the one who is pessimistic because he harms himself, but as for the one who trusts in Allah, it does not. And the purpose is not to mention these matters and the reason for their correctness sometimes and error many times, but rather the intent is that they deliberately (6) in them much lying without them indicating
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a critique by Ibn Taymiyya of false practitioners who claim knowledge of future events through various divinatory methods. He begins by recounting an incident where a judge falsely attributed an ancient origin to a book, dressing it up for a Muslim king during the siege of Acre. This introduces the broader theme: lies are more prevalent in worldly matters than in religious ones, because those who prioritize the world are more eager to deceive for worldly gain, while the people of religion have the discernment (furqan) and light from Allah to distinguish truth from falsehood. Consequently, many liars have flourished, consuming wealth unjustly and killing aspiring rulers.

Ibn Taymiyya then explains that these liars diversify their methods of deception. Sometimes they attribute their predictions to celestial motions and natural phenomena (stars, thunder, etc.)—things beyond human control. Other times, they use man-made actions like sand divination, pebble casting, barley, and lotteries with abjad letters. All these are akin to the prohibited practice of istisqam bil-azlam (divination by arrows), which was condemned in the Qur'an. The common element is that the practitioner alters physical objects to extract knowledge he does not possess. This is categorically forbidden.

In contrast, the Prophet approved of fa'l (optimism), which involves hearing a good word while acting with trust in Allah. Optimism strengthens reliance on Allah, whereas tayra (pessimism/omen-taking) opposes that reliance. Pessimism harms only the person who entertains it, while the one who trusts in Allah is unaffected.

Finally, Ibn Taymiyya clarifies his objective: not to detail the mechanics of these practices or why they sometimes hit the mark and often miss, but to expose that their practitioners deliberately lie, fabricating predictions without any genuine indication.

Key Terms
الفأل
الطيرة
الاستقسام بالأزلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what is the fundamental difference between lawful optimism (fa'l) and prohibited divination (istisqam)?
A) One uses celestial signs; the other uses man-made objects.
B) One relies on trust in Allah; the other relies on manipulating objects to extract unknown knowledge.
C) One is practiced by kings; the other by common people.
D) One is ancient; the other is modern.

Key Takeaway
The line between lawful optimism and prohibited divination is trust in Allah versus manipulating objects to claim knowledge of the unseen.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. Take a modern practice like palm reading. Identify whether it falls under the prohibited divination (istisqam) or lawful optimism (fa'l) according to Ibn Taymiyya's criteria. Explain your reasoning.
?
2. Construct a short argument explaining why the Prophet allowed fa'l but forbade tayra, using the concepts of tawakkul and istisqam.

Why Lies Flourish in Worldly Matters: Ibn Taymiyya's Epistemological Critique
Ibn Taymiyya explains why lies are more common in worldly predictions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Ibn Taymiyya's argument that lies are more prevalent in worldly predictions because those who prioritize the world lack divine discernment (furqan) and light.

Core Idea
Lack of divine guidance makes worldly predictions a breeding ground for lies.

Ibn Taymiyya observes that liars are more numerous in predicting worldly events than in religious matters. He attributes this to the absence of furqan (criterion) and light among those who prioritize the world. This lesson unpacks his epistemological reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups
Find in the text the comparison between those who give precedence to the world over religion (يُغلبون الدنيا على الدين) and the people of religion (أهل الدين).
2
Extract the two qualities of the religious
The people of religion have الفرقان بين الحق والباطل (criterion between truth and falsehood) and النور (light). Locate these in Arabic.
3
Analyze the consequence
Because worldly-minded people lack these qualities, lies increase, wealth is consumed unjustly, and many souls are killed. Connect the lack of divine guidance to harm.
