Ibn Taymiyya's Method of Hadith Criticism: Defending Yazid ibn Maysara
Ibn Taymiyya defends the hadith's chain by analyzing Yazid ibn Maysara's reliability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the criteria Ibn Taymiyya uses to defend a hadith narrator's reliability.

Core Idea
A narrator's reliability can be defended through multiple narrations, scholar acceptance, and textual clues indicating preservation.

Ibn Taymiyya not only cites the hadith but also provides a detailed defense of its chain, addressing criticisms of Yazid ibn Maysara. He employs rigorous hadith criticism methodology, demonstrating how to evaluate narrators fairly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the narrator under criticism
Yazid ibn Maysara is criticized as 'unknown in status' and only two narrators reported from him. Find where Ibn Taymiyya mentions these objections.
These are common grounds for declaring a narrator weak.
2
List Ibn Taymiyya's counterarguments
He argues: (1) Yazid is a known ascetic preacher from the Followers in Syria. (2) More than ten narrators reported from him. (3) Ibn Hibban listed him in al-Thiqat (the trustworthy). (4) Al-Hakim authenticated the hadith. (5) There is a textual clue: the narrator emphasizes direct hearing from Umm al-Darda'.
Each counterargument addresses a specific criticism.
3
Understand the principle regarding reading other scriptures
Some objected because Yazid read the books of the People of the Book. Ibn Taymiyya acknowledges this but says the hadith has a clue that protects against the suspicion that he mistakenly raised it from those books.
The clue is the detailed story about hearing directly.
4
Evaluate the overall method
Ibn Taymiyya uses multiple types of evidence: biographical (ta'dil), numerical (number of narrators), scholarly consensus (al-Hakim's authentication), and textual (qissa indicating preservation). This demonstrates a comprehensive approach.
This method is central to hadith criticism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبتدعة والآراء المخترعة، لم يكن لهم في ذلك سلف إلا رعونات النفوس المتلقاة ممَّن ساء قصده في الدين. ويروى أن الله سبحانه قال للمسيح : إني سأخلقُ أُمَّةً أفضّلُها على كل أمَّةٍ وليس لها علم ولا حِلم، فقال المسيح : أي ربِّ، كيف تفضّلهم على جميع الأمم وليس لهم علمٌ ولا حِلم؟ قال: أهبُهم من علمي وحلمي (۱). (1) أخرجه أحمد (٢٧٥٤٥) ، والبخاري في التاريخ الكبير (٣٥٥/٨)، والخرائطي في فضيلة الشكر» (۱۹)، والطبراني في «الأوسط» (٣٢٥٢) وغيرهم من حديث يزيد بن ميسرة عن أم الدرداء عن أبي الدرداء رضي اللهُ عَنْهُ مرفوعا: «إن الله عز وجل يقول: يا عيسى إني باعث من بعدك أمةً إن أصابهم ما يحبون حمدوا الله وشكروا، وإن أصابهم ما يكرهون احتسبوا وصبروا، ولا حلم ولا علم، قال: يا رب كيف هذا لهم ولا حلم ولا علم ؟ قال : أعطيهم من حلمي وعلمي». ولا بأس بإسناده، وصححه الحاكم (٣٤٨/١) ولم يتعقبه الذهبي، وحسنه البزار ٤۰۸۸) ، وابن حجر في الأمالي المطلقة» (٤٩) ، إلا أن البزار وهم في اسم راويه يزيد فجعله أخاه يونس. وأعله الألباني في الضعيفة» (٤٠٣٨، ٤٩٩١) و محققو «المسند» بأن يزيد بن ميسرة مجهول الحال لم تثبت عدالته ولم يرو عنه إلا اثنان وليس كذلك، بل هو زاهد واعظ معروف من أتباع التابعين بالشام، له أخبار كثيرة وأقوال مأثورة في «الزهد » لأبي داود (٣٩٣ - ٣٩٦) ، و ( الحلية (٢٣٤/٥ - ٢٤٣)، و«تاريخ الإسلام (٣٤٠/٣) وغيرها، وروى عنه جماعة فوق العشرة، وأورده ابن حبان في «الثقات» (٦٢٧/٧) ، ولم يَرو ما يُنْكَر، فمثله مع تصحيح الحاكم له يحسّن حديثه ما لم ينفرد بما لا يحتمل، كما قال الذهبي في الموقظة» (۷۸) : «وإن صحح له كالدارقطني والحاكم فأقل أحواله حُسْنُ حديثه». لكن قد ذُكر أنه قرأ الكتب (يعني كتب أهـل الكتاب) كما في مصنف ابن أبي شيبة» (٣٥٤۳۱)، وروى عنها كثيرًا، فيتأنى في = مروياته المرفوعة التي من هذا اللون خاصَّة، فإنها مظنَّة الوهم، لاحتمال أن تكون مما قرأه من تلك الكتب ورفعها خطاً على سبيل التوهم، كما يقعُ لغيره ممن ليس الحديث من صناعته، إلا أن في حديثه هذا قرينة تدفع عنه الوهم وتدلُّ على ضبطه له، وهي أنه قال في روايته: سمعت أم الدرداء تقول: سمعت أبا الدرداء يقول: سمعت أبا القاسم - ما سمعته يكنيه قبلها ولا بعدها ـ يقول...» ثم ذكره، وقد قال الإمام أحمد: إذا كان في الحديث قصة دلّ على أن راويه حفظه»، انظر: «هدى الساري» (٣٦٣).
The innovators and invented opinions had no predecessor in that except the foolishness of souls received from those who had evil intent in religion. And it is narrated that Allah the Exalted said to Jesus: 'I will create a nation that I will prefer over every nation, and they have no knowledge nor forbearance.' Jesus said: 'O Lord, how will You prefer them over all nations while they have no knowledge nor forbearance?' He said: 'I bestow upon them from My knowledge and My forbearance (1).' (1) Ahmad (27545), al-Bukhari in al-Tarikh al-Kabir (8/355), al-Khara'iti in Fadilat al-Shukr (19), al-Tabarani in al-Awsat (3252) and others from the hadith of Yazid ibn Maysara from Umm al-Darda' from Abu al-Darda' may Allah be pleased with him raised: 'Indeed Allah Almighty says: O Jesus, I am sending after you a nation who, if they get what they love, praise Allah and thank, and if they get what they dislike, seek reward and are patient, and there is no forbearance nor knowledge. He said: O Lord, how is this for them while they have no forbearance nor knowledge? He said: I give them from My forbearance and My knowledge.' And its chain is acceptable, al-Hakim authenticated it (1/348) and al-Dhahabi did not comment, al-Bazzar (4088) and Ibn Hajar in al-Amali al-Mutlaqah (49) deemed it good, except that al-Bazzar erred in the name of its narrator Yazid making him his brother Yunus. And al-Albani in al-Da'ifah (4038, 4991) and the editors of al-Musnad declared it weak because Yazid ibn Maysara is unknown in status, his integrity not established, and only two narrated from him, but that is not correct; rather he is a known ascetic preacher from the Followers in Syria, with many reports and sayings in al-Zuhd by Abu Dawud (393-396), al-Hilyah (5/234-243), Tarikh al-Islam (3/340) etc., and more than ten narrated from him, and Ibn Hibban mentioned him in al-Thiqat (7/627), and he did not narrate anything objectionable, so his like with al-Hakim's authentication improves his hadith as long as he does not single out something improbable, as al-Dhahabi said in al-Muqiẓah (78): 'If al-Daraqutni and al-Hakim authenticate for him, the least of his status is that his hadith is good.' But it was mentioned that he read the books (meaning books of the People of the Book) as in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah (35431), and narrated a lot from them, so one must be cautious regarding = his raised narratives of this type, for they are subject to illusion, due to the possibility that they are from what he read from those books and raised erroneously, as happens to others who are not hadith specialists, except that in this hadith there is an indication that repels the illusion and indicates his accuracy: that he said in his narration: 'I heard Umm al-Darda' say: I heard Abu al-Darda' say: I heard Abu al-Qasim - I never heard him use a kunya before or after - say...' then he mentioned it. And Imam Ahmad said: 'If there is a story in the hadith, it indicates that its narrator preserved it.' See: Huda al-Sari (363).
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a critique of innovators (ahl al-bid‘a) who rely on personal opinions rather than revelation. Ibn Taymiyya opens by stating that these innovators have no valid predecessors except the foolishness of those with evil intentions. He then cites a prophetic hadith in which Allah tells Jesus that He will create a Muslim ummah that, despite lacking intrinsic knowledge and forbearance, will be given them by Allah. This supports the idea that true knowledge and forbearance are divine gifts granted to those who follow the Prophet, not products of human intellect. The remainder of the passage is a detailed critical evaluation of the hadith's chain of narration. Ibn Taymiyya defends the narrator Yazid ibn Maysara against claims of weakness, citing multiple scholars who authenticated or deemed good the hadith, and addressing the issue that Yazid read scriptures of the People of the Book. Ibn Taymiyya argues that the hadith contains a clue (a story about hearing directly) that protects against the suspicion that it was mistakenly raised from those scriptures. Thus, the passage serves to ground the superiority of the Muslim ummah in sound prophetic tradition, undermining the claims of innovators who might rely on their own reasoning.

Key Terms
بدعة
متابعة الرسول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What clue does Ibn Taymiyya use to defend Yazid ibn Maysara's accuracy in this specific hadith?
A) Yazid was known to be a companion of the Prophet.
B) The hadith includes a story about hearing directly from Umm al-Darda'.
C) Al-Bukhari included the hadith in his Sahih.
D) Yazid never narrated any other hadith.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya demonstrates that a narrator's reliability can be defended through multiple narrations, scholar acceptance, and textual clues, even when they have read other scriptures.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Select a hadith with a disputed chain. List the criticisms against one of its narrators. Then, using Ibn Taymiyya's approach, find counterarguments that might defend the narrator's reliability (e.g., other scholars who authenticated him, textual clues).
?
Explain why Ibn Taymiyya considered the clue about direct hearing as a strong indicator of accuracy. Provide another example where a textual clue helps verify a hadith.

Parable of the Workers and Muslim Superiority
Ibn Taymiyya uses a parable to show that Muslims receive a greater reward by following the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Ibn Taymiyya uses the parable of the workers to argue that Muslim superiority comes from following the Prophet (mutaba‘a), and identify the two forms of evidence he presents.

Core Idea
Following the Prophet is the key to Allah’s extra favor, not the amount of work.

This passage is part of Ibn Taymiyya’s broader critique of the claim that Greek logic alone suffices for knowledge and reward. Here, he marshals two pieces of scriptural evidence—a Quranic promise and a prophetic parable—to show that the Muslim ummah’s superior reward is a direct result of following the Messenger, not of any rational achievement.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify Ibn Taymiyya’s central claim
Read the first sentence: 'And this is from the characteristics of following the Messenger. So the one who is more followful of him is more perfect in that.' Ibn Taymiyya asserts that the degree of perfection (kamal) corresponds to the degree of following the Prophet.
This is the thesis he will support with evidence.
2
2. Analyze the Quranic evidence
Consider the verse from Surah al-Hadid (57:28-29). It promises believers who fear Allah and believe in His Messenger a double portion of mercy, a light, and forgiveness. The verse concludes that this is to show the People of the Book that they cannot attain Allah’s bounty except through following the Messenger.
The 'double portion' (kiflain) echoes the double wage in the parable.
3
3. Analyze the parable
Examine the hadith: a man hires workers at different times. Jews work until noon (1 qirat), Christians until Asr (1 qirat), Muslims until sunset (2 qirats). The Jews and Christians complain they worked more but received less; the employer replies he did not wrong them—it is his favor to give to whom He wills.
The employer represents Allah; the different periods symbolize the times of revelation.
4
4. Connect the evidence to the claim
Both the Quranic verse and the parable teach that the Muslim ummah receives greater reward—not because of more work or longer service—but because Allah grants extra favor for following the Prophet. This supports Ibn Taymiyya’s argument that following the Prophet is the distinctive virtue that brings superiority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا من خواص متابعة الرسول، فأيهم كان له أتبع كان في ذلك أكمل، كما قال تعالى: ﴿ يَتَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا اتَّقُوا اللَّهَ وَعَامِنُوا بِرَسُولِهِ يُؤْتِكُمْ كِفْلَيْنِ مِن رَّحْمَتِهِ، وَيَجْعَل لَكُمْ نُورًا تَمْشُونَ بِهِ وَيَغْفِرْ لَكُمْ وَاللَّهُ غَفُورٌ رَّحِيمٌ ) لِئَلَّا يَعْلَمَ أَهْلُ الْكِتَبِ أَلَّا يَقْدِرُونَ عَلَى شَيْءٍ مِن فَضْلِ اللَّهِ وَأَنَّ الْفَضْلَ بِيَدِ اللَّهِ يُؤْتِيهِ مَن يَشَاءُ وَاللهُ ذُو الْفَضْلِ الْعَظِيمِ ﴾ [الحديد: ۲۸، ۲۹] . وكذلك في «الصَّحيحين» (۱) من حديث أبي موسى وعبد الله بن عمر: مَثَلُنا ومَثَلُ الأمم قبلنا كالذي استأجر أجراء، فقال: من يعمل لي إلى نصف النهار على قيراط قيراط ؟ فعَمِلَت اليهود. ثم قال: من يعمل لي إلى صلاة العصر على قيراط قيراط ؟ فعَمِلَت النصارى. ثم قال: من يعمل لي إلى غروب الشمس على قيراطين قيراطين ؟ فعَمِلَت المسلمون. فغضبت اليهود والنصارى وقالوا: نحن أكثر عملًا وأقلُّ أجرًا. قال: فهل ظلمتكم من حقكم شيئًا؟ قالوا: لا، قال: فهو فضلي أوتيه من أشاء». (1) البخاري (٥٥٧، ٥٥٨، ٢٢٦٨ ، ٢٢٦٩، ٢٢٧١، ٣٤٥٩، ٥٠٢١)، وهو من أفراده كما في الجمع بين الصحيحين» (١/ ٣١٥، ٢/ ٢٦٩).
And this is from the characteristics of following the Messenger. So the one who is more followful of him is more perfect in that, as the Exalted said: 'O you who have believed, fear Allah and believe in His Messenger; He will give you two portions of His mercy and make for you a light by which you walk and forgive you; and Allah is Forgiving and Merciful. [This is] so that the People of the Scripture may know that they are not able to attain anything from the bounty of Allah and that (all) bounty is in the hand of Allah; He gives it to whom He wills. And Allah is the possessor of great bounty.' [Al-Hadid 57:28-29]. And likewise in al-Sahihayn (1) from the hadith of Abu Musa and Abdullah ibn Umar: 'Our example and the example of the nations before us is like a man who hired laborers and said: Who will work for me until midday for a qirat each? The Jews worked. Then he said: Who will work for me until Asr prayer for a qirat each? The Christians worked. Then he said: Who will work for me until sunset for two qirats each? The Muslims worked. The Jews and Christians became angry and said: We did more work and received less wages. He said: Have I wronged you in your right? They said: No. He said: This is My favor I give to whom I will.' (1) al-Bukhari (557, 558, 2268, 2269, 2271, 3459, 5021), and it is unique to him as in al-Jam‘ bayn al-Sahihayn (1/315, 2/269).
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage continues Ibn Taymiyya's argument that the superiority of the Muslim ummah comes from following the Prophet. He first states that the more one follows the Messenger, the more perfect one becomes in this virtue. He then cites Quran 57:28-29, which promises believers who fear Allah and believe in His Messenger a double portion of mercy, a light to walk by, and forgiveness. The verse concludes that this is to show the People of the Book that they cannot attain Allah's bounty except through following the Messenger. Next, Ibn Taymiyya brings a parable from the two authentic hadith collections (al-Bukhari and Muslim) narrated by Abu Musa and Abdullah ibn Umar. In the parable, a man hires workers at different times: Jews work for one qirat until noon, Christians work for one qirat until Asr, and Muslims work for two qirats until sunset. The Jews and Christians complain that they worked more but received less, but the employer responds that he did not wrong them and that it is his favor to give to whom he wills. This illustrates that Allah gave the Muslim ummah a greater reward because they followed the Prophet, despite their shorter period of work (later revelation). The citation footnote confirms the hadith's source in al-Bukhari.

Key Terms
متابعة الرسول
قيراط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the parable of the workers in Sahihain teach about the Muslim ummah?
A) They worked the longest hours.
B) They received a lower wage than previous nations.
C) They received a double wage because of Allah's favor, not because of the amount of work.
D) They complained about their wage.

Key Takeaway
The Muslim ummah's greater reward is not due to more work but Allah's favor for following the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find another hadith or Quranic verse that uses a parable to argue for a theological or legal principle. Explain how the parable functions as evidence in the same way Ibn Taymiyya uses the workers parable.
?
In Usul al-Fiqh, the concept of 'illa (effective cause) is used to extend rulings. How does Ibn Taymiyya’s argument here about 'following the Prophet' function as a kind of 'illa for Allah’s favor? Write a brief analysis.

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Claiming Superiority over Ahl al-Hadith
Ibn Taymiyya warns against those who claim non-Hadith groups surpass Ahl al-Hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's critique against those who claim non-Hadith groups surpass Ahl al-Hadith in knowledge, and evaluate its epistemological grounds.

Core Idea
Claiming superiority over Ahl al-Hadith is either ignorant hypocrisy or pure hypocrisy.

This passage from Ibn Taymiyya's Naqd al-Mantiq is a sharp warning: anyone who asserts that philosophers or other groups have grasped hidden realities better than Ahl al-Hadith is either an ignorant hypocrite or a pure hypocrite. Ibn Taymiyya grounds this critique in Quranic proofs and the special virtue of the Prophet's followers. Understanding this critique helps us see how traditionalist scholars defended the sufficiency of revelation against rationalist encroachment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target claim
What exactly is the position Ibn Taymiyya is attacking? Find the statement in the Arabic that describes someone claiming 'a group other than the people of Hadith have grasped hidden unseen realities... above the people of Hadith'.
The claim is about epistemological superiority in knowing eschatological and metaphysical truths.
2
Extract Ibn Taymiyya's grounds
On what basis does Ibn Taymiyya reject this claim? He cites the Quran and Sunnah, the special favor given to the Prophet's followers, and a Salaf saying. Also note his use of Quran 2:13 to equate the claimants with 'fools'.
His grounds are primarily scriptural and traditional, not purely rational.
3
Classify the types of claimants
Ibn Taymiyya distinguishes two categories: (1) those who still believe in messengers but make this claim – they are ignorant with 'a strong branch of hypocrisy'; (2) those who do not believe – they are pure hypocrites. Also a third possible category: those who argue without authority (Quran 40:35).
This classification shows he is not merely dismissing but analyzing degrees of deviation.
4
Evaluate the critique's internal logic
Does Ibn Taymiyya's argument hold together? He assumes the superiority of Ahl al-Hadith is a given from revelation. The critique is not a syllogism but a rhetorical warning. Assess whether his appeal to scripture and tradition is sufficient to refute the epistemological claim.
This step requires you to think about whether the critique is convincing from a purely logical perspective or relies on authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فدلَّ الكتاب والسُّنة على أن الله يؤتي أتباعَ هذا الرَّسول من فضله ما لا يؤته لأهل الكتابين قبلهم، فكيف بمن هو دونهم من الصابئة؟ دَع مبتدعة الصَّابئة من المتفلسفة ونحوهم. ومن المعلوم أن أهل الحديث والسُّنة أخص بالرسول وأتباعه، فلهم من فضل الله وتخصيصه إيَّاهم بالعلم والحِلم وتضعيف الأجر ما ليس لغيرهم، كما قال بعضُ السَّلف: «أهل السُّنة في الإسلام كأهل الإسلام في الملل». فهذا الكلام تنبيه على ما يظنُّه أهل الجهالة والضَّلالة من نقص الصحابة في العلم والبيان، أو اليد والسِّنَان، وبسط هذا لا يحتمله هذا المقام. والمقصود التنبيه على أن كلَّ من زعَم بلسان حاله أو مقاله أن طائفةٌ غير أهل الحديث أدركوا من حقائق الأمور الباطنة الغيبية في أمر الخلق والبعث والمبدأ والمعاد، وأمر الإيمان بالله واليوم الآخر، وتعرف واجب الوجود، والنفس الناطقة، والعلوم والأخلاق التي تزكو بها النفوس وتصلح وتكمل فوق أهل الحديث، فهو إن كان من المؤمنين بالرسل فهو جاهل فيه شعبة قويةٌ من شعب النفاق، وإلا فهو منافق خالص من الذين إذا قِيلَ لَهُمْ آمِنُوا كَمَا آمَنَ النَّاسُ قَالُوا أَنُؤْمِنُ كَمَا آمَنَ السُّفَهَاءُ أَلَا إِنَّهُمْ هُمُ السُّفَهَاءُ ولكن لا يَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۳]، وقد يكون من الذين يُجَادِلُونَ فِي آيَاتِ اللهِ بِغَيْرِ سُلْطَانٍ أَتَاهُمْ [غافر: ٣٥]، ومن الذين يُحَاجُّونَ فِي اللَّهِ مِنْ بَعْدِ مَا اسْتُجِيبَ لَهُ ﴾ الآية [الشورى: ١٦].
The Book and the Sunnah indicate that Allah gives the followers of this Messenger from His bounty what He does not give to the People of the two Books before them, so how about those below them from the Sabians? Leave aside the innovating Sabians among the philosophizers and their ilk. And it is known that the people of Hadith and Sunnah are the most specific to the Messenger and his followers, so they have from Allah's bounty and His particularization of them with knowledge, forbearance, and multiplication of reward what others do not have, as some of the Salaf said: 'The people of Sunnah in Islam are like the people of Islam among the religions.' So this speech is an alert to what the people of ignorance and misguidance suppose of deficiency of the Companions in knowledge and eloquence, or in hand and spear, and expanding on this is not appropriate for this place. The intended point is an alert that whoever claims by the tongue of his state or his statement that a group other than the people of Hadith have grasped the hidden unseen realities concerning creation, resurrection, the beginning and the end, and the matter of faith in Allah and the Last Day, and the knowledge of the Necessary Existent and the rational soul, and the sciences and ethics by which souls are purified and become sound and become complete above the people of Hadith, then if he is among the believers in the messengers, he is ignorant, having a strong branch of hypocrisy, otherwise he is a pure hypocrite, from those of whom when it is said to them: 'Believe as the people have believed,' they say: 'Shall we believe as the fools have believed?' Indeed, they are the fools, but they do not know [Quran 2:13], and he may be among those who argue about the signs of Allah without any authority that has come to them [Quran 40:35], and among those who dispute concerning Allah after He has been responded to [Quran 42:16].
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a critical and warning statement by Ibn Taymiyya. He begins by asserting that the Quran and Sunnah prove that the followers of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) receive more divine favor than earlier religious communities, let alone the Sabians and philosophizers. He then emphasizes that Ahl al-Hadith (the people of Hadith) are the most closely associated with the Prophet and his Companions, and therefore they have exclusive blessings in knowledge, forbearance, and multiplied reward. He quotes a Salaf saying to illustrate their elevated status. The warning targets those who ignorantly suppose the Companions lacked knowledge or strength. The core warning is against anyone who claims that any group other than Ahl al-Hadith have attained deeper hidden realities about creation, resurrection, faith, and ethics, surpassing them. Ibn Taymiyya classifies such claimants as either ignorant and partially hypocritical if they believe in messengers, or pure hypocrites, citing Quranic verses about those who reject faith and argue without authority.

Key Terms
أهل الحديث
الصابئة
النفاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what is the status of a person who claims that philosophers have attained superior hidden knowledge to Ahl al-Hadith?
A) He is a true believer with a valid opinion.
B) He is either an ignorant person with a branch of hypocrisy or a pure hypocrite.
C) He is a disbeliever without any faith.
D) He is a mujtahid deserving reward.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's critique establishes that claiming superiority over Ahl al-Hadith in knowledge of unseen realities is a sign of hypocrisy, rooted in ignorance of the Quranic evidence for their special status.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task: Take a hypothetical claim: 'Philosophers have discovered, through reason alone, that the soul is immaterial and survives death, surpassing what Ahl al-Hadith have transmitted from the Prophet.' Apply Ibn Taymiyya's critique: First, identify the two categories of claimants he would assign. Second, write a one-paragraph counter-argument using his grounds from Quran and Sunnah.

Discerning Truth and Falsehood in al-'Izz's Classification
Author critiques al-'Izz's classification of Hashwiyya, exposing its truth and falsehood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the truth and falsehood in al-'Izz's classification of Hashwiyya according to Ibn Taymiyya's critique.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya accepts condemnation of anthropomorphism but rejects false claims of Salaf authority.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya applies a critical method to a classification of the Hashwiyya. He shows that an apparent dichotomy may contain both valid and invalid components. By learning to separate these, you will develop the skill to evaluate theological classifications rigorously, a tool essential for navigating debates in 'aqida and usul al-din.

Guided Path
1
Identify the classification under critique
Find the two types of Hashwiyya as described by al-'Izz: one openly anthropomorphist, the other hiding behind the Salaf. Note that Ibn Taymiyya quotes this classification at the start.
2
Separate truth from falsehood
Ibn Taymiyya explicitly states the classification contains both truth and falsehood. Identify the truth: condemnation of those who liken God to creation, supported by Quranic verses. Identify the falsehood: the claim that the second group truly follows the Salaf while being ignorant or deviant.
Use the verses cited: 42:11, 112:4, 19:65.
3
Examine the evidence and its strength
Note that Ibn Taymiyya asserts he has provided stronger rational proofs against anthropomorphism than those who claim tanzih. He criticizes their arguments as weak because they mix truth and falsehood. This shows his epistemological standard: proof must be consistent and free from corruption.
Contrast his method with the 'weak proofs' of the self-proclaimed tanzih group.
4
Assess Ibn Taymiyya's alternative
He advocates for moderate speech and seeking correct saying (sadid), citing 33:70-71. He also condemns fabricated hadiths that extremists use to support anthropomorphism. This completes his critique: he reaffirms tawhid and tanzih without the errors of either extreme.
Examples of fabricated hadiths: sweat of horses, descent on camel, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل وأما قول من قال: «إن الحشوية على ضربين: أحدهما: لا يتحاشى من الحشو والتشبيه والتجسيم. والآخر يتستر بمذهب السلف ومذهب السلف إنما هو التوحيد والتنزيه، دون التشبيه والتجسيم» وكذا جميع المبتدعة يزعمون أنهم على مذهب السلف، كما قال القائل: وكل يدعون وصل ليلى وليلى لا تقر لهم بذاكا فهذا الكلام فيه حق وباطل. فمن الحق الذي فيه: ذم من مثل الله بمخلوقاته ويجعل صفاته من جنس صفاتهم، وقد قال الله تعالى: لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ [الشورى: 11] وقال تعالى: وَلَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ كُفُوًا أَحَدٌ [الإخلاص: 4]، وقال: هَلْ تَعْلَمُ لَهُ سَمِيًّا [مريم: 65]. وقد بسطنا القول في ذلك وذكرنا الدلالات العقلية التي دل عليها كتاب في نفي ذلك، وبينا منه ما لم تذكره النفاة الذين يتسمون بالتنزيه ولا يوجد في كتبهم ولا يسمع من أئمتهم، بل عامة حججهم التي يذكرونها حجج ضعيفة؛ لأنهم يقصدون إثبات حق وباطل، فلا يقوم على ذلك حجة مطردة سليمة عن الفساد، بخلاف من اقتصد في قوله وتحرّى القول السديد فإن الله يصلح عمله كما قال تعالى: يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا اتَّقُوا اللَّهَ وَقُولُوا قَوْلًا سَدِيدًا يُصْلِحْ لَكُمْ أَعْمَالَكُمْ وَيَغْفِرْ لَكُمْ ذُنُوبَكُمْ [الأحزاب: 70-71]. وفيه من الحق الإشارة إلى الرد على من انتحل مذهب السلف مع الجهل بمقالهم، أو المخالفة لهم بزيادة أو نقصان. فتمثيل الله بخلقه والكذب على السلف من الأمور المنكرة، سواء سمي ذلك حشوا أو لم يسم، وهذا يتناول كثيرًا من غالية المثبتة الذين يروون أحاديث موضوعة في الصفات، مثل حديث عرق الخيل، ونزوله عشية عرفة على الجمل الأورق حتى يصافح المشاة ويعانق الركبان، وتجليه لنبيه في الأرض، أو رؤيته له على كرسي بين السماء والأرض، أو رؤيته إياه في الطواف
Section. As for the statement of one who said: 'Indeed, the Hashwiyya are of two types: one does not refrain from anthropomorphism, comparison, and corporealism; the other screens himself behind the way of the Salaf, while the way of the Salaf is only tawhid and tanzih, without comparison and corporealism.' Likewise, all innovators claim that they follow the way of the Salaf, as the poet said: 'And all claim the union with Layla, but Layla does not acknowledge them for that.' So this speech contains truth and falsehood. Among the truth in it is: condemnation of one who likens God to His creatures and makes His attributes of the same kind as their attributes, and Allah Almighty said: 'There is nothing like unto Him' [Ash-Shura 42:11], and He said: 'And there is none comparable to Him' [Al-Ikhlas 112:4], and He said: 'Do you know of any similarity to Him?' [Maryam 19:65]. And we have elaborated on that and mentioned the intellectual proofs that the Book indicates for negating that, and we explained from it what the negators who call themselves 'tanzih' did not mention; it is not found in their books nor heard from their imams. Rather, most of their arguments that they mention are weak, because they aim to prove truth and falsehood together, so no consistent proof free from corruption is established thereby, unlike one who is moderate in his speech and seeks the correct saying, for Allah will set right his deed, as He said: 'O you who have believed, fear Allah and speak words of right direction. He will set right for you your deeds and forgive you your sins' [Al-Ahzab 33:70-71]. And within it is the truth of pointing to refutation of those who adopt the way of the Salaf while ignorant of their statements, or oppose them by addition or deficiency. So likening Allah to His creation and lying about the Salaf are objectionable matters, whether that is called hashw or not. And this includes many of the extremist affirmers who narrate fabricated hadiths about the attributes, such as the hadith of the sweat of the horses, and His descent on the evening of 'Arafa on the dappled camel until He shakes hands with pedestrians and embraces riders, and His manifestation to His prophet on earth, or his seeing Him on a throne between heaven and earth, or his seeing Him during the tawaf.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of a classification of the Hashwiyya (a term often used pejoratively for those accused of crude anthropomorphism) attributed to al-'Izz ibn Abd al-Salam. The author, Ibn Taymiyya, begins by quoting the statement that the Hashwiyya are of two types: one openly embraces hashw (crude speech), tashbih (comparison), and tajsim (corporealism); the other hides behind the authority of the Salaf, while the true Salafi way is tawhid (divine unity) and tanzih (transcendence). Ibn Taymiyya then comments that this statement contains both truth and falsehood. The truth is the condemnation of those who liken God to His creatures, supported by Quranic verses: 'There is nothing like unto Him' (42:11), 'none comparable to Him' (112:4), 'do you know of any similarity to Him?' (19:65). He then asserts that he has elaborated on the intellectual proofs for negating such comparison, surpassing the arguments of those who claim tanzih but whose proofs are weak. Their weakness stems from aiming to prove both truth and falsehood, leading to inconsistency. He contrasts them with the moderate person who seeks correct speech, citing verse 33:70-71 on the reward for right speech. The passage also identifies the truth in the original statement as pointing to refutation of those who falsely claim to follow the Salaf while being ignorant or deviating. He then condemns likening Allah to creation and lying about the Salaf, regardless of labeling. He specifically criticizes extremists (ghaliya al-muthbita) who narrate fabricated hadiths, giving examples: the hadith of the sweat of horses, God's descent on a camel at 'Arafa shaking hands, and visions of God on a throne or during tawaf. This passage demonstrates Ibn Taymiyya's method of dissecting a claim to separate its valid criticisms from its errors, using Quranic evidence and rational critique.

Key Terms
الحشوية
التشبيه
التنزيه
مذهب السلف

B) The condemnation of those who liken God to His creatures.
C) The claim that the second group follows the Salaf.
D) The use of the term 'Hashwiyya' for all literalists.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya affirms the condemnation of anthropomorphism as truth but rejects the false attribution of Salaf authority to the second group.

Examine a contemporary classification of Muslims into 'literalists' and 'metaphorical interpreters.' Identify what each side affirms and negates, and assess whether the classification mixes truth and falsehood as Ibn Taymiyya did.

Ibn Taymiyya's critique of fabricated hadiths on divine attributes
Ibn Taymiyya criticizes those who fabricate hadiths describing Allah in corporeal terms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two-pronged critique Ibn Taymiyya makes against fabricated hadiths on divine attributes: theological error (tamthīl) and methodological error (lying about the Salaf).

Core Idea
Fabricated hadiths corrupt both theology and methodology.

Ibn Taymiyya is not rejecting all hadiths about the attributes of Allah; he is drawing a sharp line between authentic reports and fabricated ones. In this passage, he exposes the double fault of extreme anthropomorphists: they commit theological error by likening Allah to creation (tamthīl), and they commit methodological error by falsely attributing statements to the early Muslims (al-Salaf). Understanding this critique trains you to evaluate the source quality of hadiths used in theological arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two principal errors
Locate the first sentence: 'So likening Allah to His creation and lying about the Salaf are reprehensible matters.' Ibn Taymiyya condemns two things: tamthīl (theological error) and lying about the Salaf (methodological error). These are the pillars of his critique.
2
Find the fabricated examples
Read the list: 'sweat of the horses', 'descending on a camel at Arafah', 'seeing Allah on a throne between heaven and earth', etc. These are concrete instances of the error. Ask yourself: What do they have in common? They ascribe physical, bodily actions to Allah.
All are 'mawḍūʿah' (fabricated) – a technical term in hadith criticism.
3
Understand the label 'ghāliyat al-muthbitah'
Ibn Taymiyya names the perpetrators: 'extreme affirmers of attributes' – those who go beyond the moderate affirmation of the Salaf. They claim to defend the attributes but end up with anthropomorphism.
This is a polemical label; not all affirmers of attributes are extreme.
4
Apply the critique to a new example
Imagine someone today claims a hadith that 'Allah has a shadow'. Use Ibn Taymiyya's two criteria: does it involve tamthīl? Is it fabricating something about the Salaf? Assess its authenticity using hadith criticism principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فتمثيلُ الله بخلقه والكذب على السَّلف من الأمور المنكرة، سواء سمي ذلك حشوا أو لم يُسَمَّ، وهذا يتناول كثيرًا من غالية المثبتة الذين يروون أحاديث موضوعةٌ في الصَّفات، مثل حديث عَرَق الخيل، ونزوله عشية عرفة على الجمل الأورق حتى يصافح المُشَاة ويعانق الركبان، وتجليه لنبيه في الأرض، أو رؤيته له على كرسي بين السماء والأرض، أو رؤيته إياه في الطواف أو في بعض سكك المدينة، إلى غير ذلك من الأحاديث الموضوعة.
So likening Allah to His creation and lying about the Salaf are reprehensible matters, whether called 'hashw' or not. And this includes many of the extreme affirmers who narrate fabricated hadiths about the attributes, such as the hadith of the 'sweat of the horses', and His descending on the evening of Arafah on a dappled camel until He shakes hands with pedestrians and embraces the riders, and His manifesting to His Prophet on earth, or his seeing Him on a throne between heaven and earth, or his seeing Him during the circumambulation or in some alleys of Medina, and other fabricated hadiths.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is a critique by Ibn Taymiyya of those who attribute to Allah anthropomorphic characteristics through fabricated hadiths. He begins by stating that likening Allah to His creation (tamthil) and lying about the Salaf (the early pious Muslims) are unacceptable, regardless of whether such extreme anthropomorphism is labeled 'hashw' (crude literalism) or not. He then specifies that this criticism targets the 'ghaliyah al-muthbitah' (extreme affirmers of attributes), who go beyond the proper affirmation of divine attributes by narrating spurious reports that describe Allah in corporeal terms—such as the hadith about the 'sweat of the horses' (referring to a fabricated story about the creation of horses from Allah's sweat), or Allah descending on a camel at Arafah, or the Prophet seeing Allah in various earthly settings like a throne, the Tawaf, or the streets of Medina. Ibn Taymiyya dismisses these as 'mawdu'ah' (fabricated) and implies that they are both theologically erroneous and a slander against the Salaf, who never taught such things. This passage reflects Ibn Taymiyya's broader polemic against deviation in theology and his insistence on adhering to authentic revelation and the consensus of the early Muslims.

Key Terms
تمثيل
موضوعة
غالية المثبتة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya in this passage, what is the status of hadiths like 'the sweat of the horses' or 'descending on a camel'?
A) They are authentic and should be accepted literally.
B) They are fabricated and represent a grave sin.
C) They are metaphorical and require interpretation.
D) They are weak but can be used as evidence.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya condemns fabricated hadiths on divine attributes on two grounds: they commit tamthīl (likening Allah to creation) and they falsely attribute statements to the Salaf, thereby combining theological and methodological error.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Create a brief argument that a certain hadith on attributes is acceptable according to Ibn Taymiyya's criteria: it must be authentic and free from tamthīl.
